Industry and Commerce Loan Association Continues to Approve Loans, Totaling RMB 12,900 85

The Shanghai Industry and Commerce Loan Review Committee held its 28th meeting at the China National Goods Bank on Tianjin Road at 4:30 PM on the 29th. Committee members present included Cai Zengji, Song Ziliang, Bei Songshen, Xi Demao, Xiaolai, Du Yuesheng (represented by Wang), Qin Runqing, Wang Yansong, and Zhang Peishen (represented by Xi). Chairman Cai Zengji reported on the daily affairs of the association. Ten applications for small credit loans were submitted, and after review, it was decided to approve loans totaling RMB 12,900. Twelve other applications were rejected because their businesses did not meet the loan principles or because the intended use of the loans did not comply with the regulations. The applicants will be notified of the decisions. According to the association's authorities, whom a reporter from Xin Xin She interviewed yesterday, although newspaper reports and repeated verbal instructions from the association's staff have emphasized that the application amount should not exceed half of the capital, as stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, there are still those who falsely fill out the forms in an attempt to borrow more money. However, their efforts are futile. Every application received by the association is first reviewed by representatives of various banks. If it is deemed loanable, it will be investigated. After the investigation is completed, it will be reviewed again before being submitted to the meeting for review and decision. Although the process takes a little longer, it is necessary to be careful in handling public funds. Therefore, all applications that do not comply with the Ministry's regulations will be rejected, and those who falsely report their capital will have their loan amounts reduced. To reiterate, those who wish to apply for a loan should go to the association's office upstairs at the China National Goods Bank on Tianjin Road to obtain a form. Be sure to inquire about the procedures in detail and do not follow the path of deceiving yourself and others.

British-Owned Meihua Bank Closed Yesterday Afternoon, Failed in Efforts to Raise Funds to Resume Business, Chinese Manager Absconded, Auditors Hired to Audit Accounts 86

According to Xin Sheng She, the British-owned Meihua Bank, which officially opened on April 8, specializing in all banking business with a capital of RMB 1 million registered in Hong Kong, has not joined the Foreign Bankers Association or the Shanghai Banking Association. After a run on the bank occurred a few days ago, it temporarily suspended business on the 28th. Chairman Jairo and others tried to raise funds and originally planned to resume business at 2:30 PM yesterday afternoon. However, due to the failure to raise funds and the absconding of Chinese manager Gu Yubo and Chinese deputy manager Zhang Xusheng, they were unable to cope with the situation.

Emergency Meeting: Chairman Jairo, foreign manager Meng Li, and foreign deputy manager Like held an emergency meeting at the bank at 1:00 PM yesterday. They decided to hire auditors to audit the accounts and temporarily suspend business. The original plan to resume business at 2:30 PM was cancelled, and the front and rear doors were closed tightly at 2:00 PM with an announcement of the suspension of business. The bank has deposits of RMB 77,699 (80-90% of which are from Chinese customers) and issued promissory notes worth RMB 86,922 (mostly held by Chinese customers). It is said that the amount of loans made is also considerable.

Notice of Closure: After temporarily suspending business at 2:00 PM yesterday afternoon, Meihua Bank posted a notice in both Chinese and English at the entrance. The original text of the Chinese notice is as follows: "Due to the discovery of significant irregularities by the Chinese manager and responsible personnel of this bank, who have absconded, it has been decided at an emergency meeting to hire auditors to audit the accounts and temporarily suspend payments. All deposits (RMB 77,699 and checks worth RMB 86,922) will be returned after verification. This is hereby announced. The amount owed to people exceeds the number of people owed."

Agricultural Foundation Bureau's Outline Slightly Modified, Capital Increased to 60 Million Yuan, Minister Wu to Convene Second Discussion Meeting the Day After Tomorrow 87

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce plans to establish an Agricultural Foundation Bureau to rescue rural areas and revive industry. After obtaining the consent of the Shanghai banking community, it has formulated a general outline of measures and is now soliciting opinions from the banking community in order to formulate detailed organizational measures. It has been learned that the original outline has been slightly modified, and the banks have been notified to convene a meeting on the 2nd to discuss everything. Details are as follows:

Soliciting Opinions: When Minister of Industry and Commerce Wu Dingchang first convened the banking community to discuss the establishment of the Agricultural Foundation Bureau, many bankers were unable to attend due to the spring holidays. The Bankers Association sent a letter to various banks to solicit their opinions, which were to be sent to the association by May 15 so that they could be compiled and sent to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. A general meeting will then be convened to discuss the implementation.

Increasing Capital: Minister Wu came to Shanghai a few days ago and invited bankers who study agricultural economics, including Zou Bingwen, Wang Zhixin, Zhang Xinyi, and Li Zhongchu, to discuss the matter. The original outline of measures was modified. The bureau's capital was originally set at 30 million yuan, with the government allocating 6 million yuan annually for five years. The circulating funds had no fixed amount and would be invested by participating banks. Now, the fixed capital has been increased to 60 million yuan, with the government contributing 30 million yuan, which will still be allocated over five years. The remaining 30 million yuan will be called joint venture capital and will be paid by participating banks over five years.

Adding Directors: The bureau originally had 13 directors, but this has now been increased to 21. The government will select 11 directors, and participating banks will nominate 10 directors. Other articles have also been modified and have now been sent by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to the Bankers Association for distribution to various banks for their information so that they can propose their opinions based on the outline. It has also been learned that Minister Wu will convene a second discussion meeting on the afternoon of the 2nd, and the association has notified the banks to send representatives to attend.

A Proof of Inaccurate Metering by the Concession Telephone Company, Handling Registration for Disconnecting Users, Charging Fees for Phones Not Yet Installed 88

According to Da Gong She, due to the illegal price increase by the Shanghai Telephone Company, telephone users in the Special District of Shanghai cannot afford it and are disconnecting their phones. The Telephone Problem Committee is compiling statistics on the number of disconnections in order to make an effective protest. Yesterday, it specifically notified users in various districts that all users who have disconnected their phones in opposition to the telephone price increase should register with the committee within two weeks. Details are as follows:

Disconnected Users Quickly Register:

Yesterday, the Telephone Problem Committee of the Special District issued a notice to all telephone users who have disconnected their phones: "Since the Shanghai Telephone Company implemented an illegal price increase, society has been in turmoil. We have repeatedly negotiated with the Municipal Council to request measures to stop it. However, the Municipal Council has used the signed franchise agreement as the basis, ignoring the calls of society, which is regrettable. Now, users in various districts, in order to resist the company's unreasonable price increase, have refused to pay fees and are disconnecting their phones. In order to clarify the number of disconnections so as to make an effective protest, we hereby notify all users in various districts that if they have disconnected their phones in opposition to the company's price increase, they should fill in the phone number, account name, and damage comparison table within two weeks and send them to the Telephone Problem Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in the Tianhou Palace. This matter concerns the public interest, so please do not delay."

Report Company's Inaccurate Metering:

Yesterday, the committee received a letter from Shenzhou Pharmacy at 492 Tianjin Road, which stated: "Our pharmacy installed a phone on April 6. On the 26th, we received a bill from the Shanghai Telephone Company, which stated that there was a call to the Chinese area on March 22, costing 5 cents. We checked and found that our pharmacy had not yet installed a phone in March, so how could there be a call? We sent someone to negotiate with the company, and an employee named Wei admitted that the metering was incorrect and agreed to cancel the charge. This shows that the company's usual metering is indeed inaccurate. In addition to refusing to pay the fee and sending a letter to the company to disconnect the phone immediately, we are writing to your committee to investigate and ask you to launch a firm protest in order to achieve the goal of canceling the unreasonable per-call metering."

Various Industries Stably Weather the End of April Period; Most Expiring Loans are Rolled Over; New Loans and Recovered Loans are Few 89

Yesterday marked the end of the fourth month period for industrial and commercial loans in Shanghai. The long-term credit loans extended by various banks and firms to industrial and commercial enterprises, which amounted to a total of 50 million yuan, were mostly held by money shops. In order to tighten credit, the various banks and firms originally intended to recover a portion of these loans. However, upon the request of the borrowing industrial and commercial firms, they were granted a special rollover to the end of October. The borrowers paid the interest in full, but the amount recovered was only about 10 to 20 percent. As for the loans extended in Shanghai by Ningbo banks, which amounted to a total of 15 million yuan, many Ningbo banks had closed down after the financial turmoil. Therefore, there was an intention to recover all these loans, but in the end, only 20 to 30 percent were recovered. Moreover, many money shops had already closed down themselves, and their loans had not yet been recovered.

Very Few New Loans Extended Money shops mostly extend long-term loans for six months, with periods ending in late April and late October each year. The interest rates are higher from November to April due to supply and demand, and slightly lower from May to October. The monthly interest rates vary from 8.5% to 1.5%, depending on the borrower's creditworthiness. This year, all money shops have uniformly tightened credit, so the amount of new long-term credit loans extended at the end of April was very small. Moreover, the spring silk and new wheat will soon be on the market, and the various money shops are particularly cautious about extending credit for silk and wheat purchases. However, fourteen banks, including the Bank of Communications, have jointly established a syndicate to handle a large-scale 30 million yuan loan for silk purchases.

Various Banks and Firms are Cautious About Discounting Bills

Yesterday, the various money shops were particularly busy with the collection and settlement of accounts for the end of April. Internal office hours were also extended. The interest on fixed deposits of various shareholders was settled according to the internal market rates. The call loan rate in the money market yesterday was still 8% per thousand yuan per day. The reason for this is that the various banks and firms are particularly cautious about discounting bills in order to avoid risks. They will not discount bills from non-creditworthy counterparts and prefer to deposit most of their funds in reserve. As for the Joint Reserve Committee of Banks and the Joint Reserve Treasury of Money Shops, they have ample reserves and are making every effort to regulate the finances of member banks and money shops.

Bureau of Industry and Commerce and Rickshaw Merchants Discuss Outstanding Cases Yesterday; The Public Works Department Decides to Reduce Rent According to Regulations; the Bureau Agrees in Principle to Reorganize the Mutual Aid Society 92

The Public Works Department of the Public Settlement and rickshaw merchants held a joint meeting at the Public Works Department at 9:45 AM yesterday to resolve disputes in the rickshaw industry. The Public Works Department was represented by Fessenden, Phillips, Massey, Hodekui, and Zhu Maocheng, and the rickshaw merchants were represented by Yin Zhiling, Hou Shaoan, Gu Songmao, Kunyi, and Ma Xianshi. Fessenden chaired the meeting. First, Yin Zhiling, the representative of the rickshaw merchants, stated the opinions of the rickshaw merchants: 1. Regarding the rent reduction issue, it is believed that the Public Works Department violated the "86 Agreement" of 1934. Rickshaws in the Public Settlement have licenses from the Chinese, French, and British settlements. The Public Works Department of the Public Settlement has no right to unilaterally stipulate rickshaw rent. Rickshaw rent is equivalent to general housing rent and land rent, and cannot be compared with the relationship between public buses and passengers. It is questionable whether the Public Works Department has the right to stipulate it. The rickshaw merchants cannot maintain their capital. The representative of the Public Works Department stated that although the rickshaw merchants' statements were very reasonable, the Public Works Department's regulations on rickshaw rent are based on the license regulations, and the 1934 agreement is not enough to restrict the Public Works Department's changes. The Public Works Department believes that it has the right to stipulate license regulations and has the right to consider issuing licenses to those who obey the license regulations at any time, and is unwilling to consider other issues. The rickshaw merchants stated that they reserve the right to protest so that they can negotiate at any time. 2. Regarding the Mutual Aid Society issue, the rickshaw merchants stated that since the Mutual Aid Society is not a charitable organization, the Public Works Department should not interfere. Now the rickshaw pullers have stated that they are unwilling to continue paying the mutual aid fee, and the rickshaw owners are only willing to pay the license fee of 2 yuan and 9 cents from next month and stop collecting the mutual aid fee on their behalf. However, the Public Works Department did not provide a reply in its letter to the rickshaw merchants, which means it is acquiescing. The representative of the Public Works Department replied that it was not acquiescing, but hoped to discuss it as much as possible at the meeting. The Public Works Department believes that it is very difficult to abolish the Mutual Aid Society immediately, but if the rickshaw merchants have a more complete solution, the Public Works Department is willing to accept it. The representative of the rickshaw merchants stated that the Mutual Aid Society's charging of fees to rickshaw pullers is contrary to the original purpose of helping rickshaw pullers, and the undertakings of the Mutual Aid Society have caused disputes due to their lack of universality. In the future, funds should be allocated separately for the Mutual Aid Fee. If the Public Works Department is unwilling to bear this expense, the rickshaw merchants are willing to bear it. However, in the future, the work of the Mutual Aid Society should be handled by a third party who is unrelated to both the Public Works Department and the rickshaw merchants so that it can be fair and impartial. The representative of the Public Works Department believes that this proposal is very sympathetic. If it is chaired by a public third party and the economy is guaranteed, the Public Works Department is very sympathetic. However, specific measures need to be discussed with the representatives of the rickshaw merchants. The rickshaw merchants stated how to deal with the problem of license donation in May if rickshaw pullers do not pay the Mutual Aid Society fee. The Public Works Department stated that the old regulations are still valid before the new regulations are implemented. The rickshaw merchants believe that how to deal with it if rickshaw pullers are unwilling to pay. The Public Works Department replied that if rickshaw pullers are unwilling to pay, rickshaw merchants should urge them to pay. The rickshaw merchants stated that this point needs to be solicited from all rickshaw pullers before a decision can be made. 3. Registration of rickshaw pullers. The rickshaw merchants claimed that the Public Works Department has not yet indicated how many rickshaw pullers are limited. The Public Works Department once stated that it authorized the rickshaw committee to register the number of people required by the rickshaw merchants, but the rickshaw committee caused disputes because it failed to register as much as possible. The chairman of the rickshaw committee, Massey, replied that the rickshaw committee is only prepared to continue registering 5,000 people. If the allocation is insufficient, the rickshaw committee will handle it directly. At this point, it was already 12 o'clock, so the meeting adjourned.

Notice to Rickshaw Owners The Special Zone Rickshaw Industry Association issued a notice to all rickshaw owners yesterday, stating that regarding the Mutual Aid Society issue, the association previously received a request from the rickshaw puller representatives in each district to stop paying the Mutual Aid Fee, etc., and reported the situation to the Public Works Department. According to the results of the association's representatives attending the Public Works Department meeting, although the Public Works Department promised to reorganize the Mutual Aid Society, specific plans are still to be discussed. The association believes that the Mutual Aid Fee should continue to be paid, and the opinions of all rickshaw pullers should be solicited separately as a basis. However, the Mutual Aid Fee from May 1st to 6th was originally paid on behalf of the rickshaw owners when they received their licenses in April, so the rickshaw owners are still unable to collect it. A solution will be reached after all rickshaw pullers express their opinions. As for the license fee for May, all rickshaw owners should deposit 5 yuan and 1 jiao per license at the Jiangxi Road Shanghai Bank Trust Department before May 2nd to resolve the issue before donating the license to operate. Regarding the rickshaw puller registration issue, the Public Works Department stated that it will not allow an increase in the number of rickshaw pullers until the exact number of rickshaw pullers is known. The association has printed forms and distributed them to each zhuo hang to conduct a thorough investigation and fill them out, and to test the opinions of all rickshaw pullers on the Mutual Aid Society. The forms should also be filled out and submitted to the association before May 4th for review. This notice is hereby issued for lack of thoroughness.

Bureau Report According to the report of the person in charge of the Public Works Department, the main point of yesterday's negotiations was the future of the rickshaw puller Mutual Aid Society. First, the rickshaw merchants requested a reorganization. The representative of the bureau immediately stated that the current organization of the council of the society was decided at the June meeting last year, which included representatives from rickshaw pullers, rickshaw merchants, municipal merchants associations, Chinese taxpayers associations, rickshaw committee, and social service committee. The organization is quite complete, and the current plan is the result of the rickshaw committee's deep consideration of all issues. However, the Public Works Department is willing to sincerely consider any reorganization plan for the Mutual Aid Society that can guarantee that the revenue will not be shaken, the person in charge of management should be willing to work hard and devote himself to increasing the happiness of members, and can obtain the satisfaction of the Bureau. Before this plan is submitted and passed, the Public Works Department will give priority to rickshaw merchants who are willing to continue cooperating in collecting the Mutual Aid Society fee when issuing licenses. If a rickshaw merchant insists on his own opinion, the Public Works Department may no longer continue his license and the rickshaw committee will decide to issue it. Other rickshaw owners and merchant representatives asked whether the bureau would object if the Mutual Aid Society was separated from the Public Works Department and became independent. The representative of the Public Works Department replied that the bureau does not object to this plan, but this plan should be considered satisfactory by the Public Works Department and be able to guarantee the above two conditions. Then, the two sides discussed the number of rickshaw pullers to be registered. The representative of the Bureau reiterated the previous proposal that it is willing to register a sufficient number of people according to the needs of the rickshaw industry, but the rickshaw merchants should cooperate as a prerequisite, that is, the rickshaw merchants can quickly recommend the 5,000 rickshaw pullers that the rickshaw committee has now decided to register.

Eurasia Aviation Corporation and the Nanking-Shanghai-Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau have signed a contract to launch land-air intermodal transportation, which will be implemented starting today. Seven Banks Including Bank of Communications Continued to Discuss Spring Silk Loan Regulations Yesterday; Xinhua, Quanye, and Zhizhong Three Banks Join Cooperation 98

Fourteen banks, including the Bank of Communications, have jointly formed a syndicate for spring 1925 silk acquisition and loan. Italy Restricts the Import of Banknotes or Securities 99

According to the Central News Agency, Shanghai Postal Administration Notice No. 1319 states that according to a letter from the Italian Postal Administration, banknotes issued by this country's banks or securities issued by the government may not be imported from abroad into this country's territory without the approval of the Ministry of Finance, except for banknotes and securities sent by mail from formally stationed foreign correspondence traders (banking operators) to banks or banking operators in this country or its territory. This has been stipulated by the Ministry of Finance's order of October 3, 1935, and it should be noted that it is now notified for general knowledge. This is a notice from the Director-General, J.P. O'Malley, April 27th.

Salt Tax Revenue Did Not Decrease in the First Three Months of This Year 104

According to news from the Salt Revenue Audit Office of the Ministry of Finance, reports from Nanjing communications stated that the salt tax revenue for January, February, and March of this year had slightly decreased compared to the same period last year. This was said to be due to the widespread sale of refined salt inland and the double impact of smuggling in various regions. Now, according to a spokesperson from the Salt Revenue Audit Office, the tax revenue for January, February, and March of this year has not decreased, but has slightly increased. It is even more unfounded to say that allowing refined salt to be sold inland has reduced tax revenue, as refined and coarse salt are taxed at the same rate, which should not affect the total salt tax revenue.

Forging a Chop to Illegally Obtain Remittance Jin Wenkai Yields to Greed 113

Wang Rugui, a Shandong native residing in a bungalow behind Fudan University in Jiangwan, has been doing yellow sand and gravel business in Shanghai. He is friendly with Jin Wenkai (a Hunan native), the owner of a pancake shop at No. 55 Luban Road in the South City. When there are family letters to be sent, they are often sent to the pancake shop for Jin to forward. In the middle of this month, a registered mail was sent from Wang's home in Shandong, containing a remittance check for 15 yuan, which was to be received and opened by Wang Rugui. However, after Jin received the registered mail, he secretly opened it. Seeing the 15 yuan remittance check, he had malicious intentions. He secretly did not tell Wang, but went to a seal engraving shop to engrave a chop with the three characters of Wang Rugui, stamped it on the remittance check, and secretly went to the post office to withdraw the 15 yuan for his own use. Later, after Wang investigated and found out the truth, he questioned Jin. Jin's words were evasive, and he refused to hand over the remittance. Wang then reported to the police and took Jin to the Ximen Public Security Branch Bureau. The Third Section of the General Bureau transferred the case to the local court for interrogation.

Shangqiao Yanjiakou Farmer Murder Case Verdict Chen Huangshi, Lu Ziliang, and Others All Found Not Guilty Only Need to Provide Substantial Shop Guarantees and Cash Guarantees 114

Chen Mingfu, a farmer from Chongming living in Yanjiakou, Gaoqiao, Pudong, was murdered on the night of November 21 last year, and his body was abandoned on the riverbank. After Inspector Li Fen of the local court arrived at the scene and determined the cause of death, Chen Huangshi, the wife of the deceased, and Lu Ziliang, the maternal uncle of the deceased, were interrogated on suspicion of jointly committing the murder, and a public prosecution was filed. Cai Dingcheng, the head of the criminal court, repeatedly conducted open trials. Considering that the case involved major discrepancies, he spared no effort in seeking details and repeatedly summoned witnesses for thorough and intensive trials. All circumstances have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the verdict was announced. At that time, Judge Cai arrived at the Criminal Court No. 3, and ordered Chen Huangshi, Lu Ziliang, and others in custody to be brought to the case. Lu Jianai, the defendant's lawyer, also appeared in court at the same time. Judge Cai briefly questioned them a few words, then stood up and announced the verdict: Chen Huangshi and Lu Ziliang were both found not guilty and allowed to be released on bail. However, due to the seriousness of the case, Lu Ziliang must provide three substantial shop guarantees and bear a written guarantee of 10,000 yuan, and Chen Huangshi must provide two substantial shop guarantees and a written guarantee of 5,000 yuan. Attorney Lu Jianai listened to the verdict and stood up, requesting the court to reduce the guarantee and stating that it was not easy to find three shop guarantees at once, and requesting that it be changed to one shop guarantee. Judge Cai instructed that the case was still subject to appeal by the prosecutor and should be handled with caution. He changed Lu Ziliang to two shop guarantees and reduced the guarantee to 8,000 yuan, and Chen Huangshi to two shop guarantees and reduced the guarantee to 4,000 yuan. After the judgment, they were returned to custody separately, pending the completion of the bail procedures before they were allowed to be released on bail.

Prostitute Brothel Owner Sues Xu Qizhong Case Three Promissory Notes Totaling 10,000 Yuan Trial Concluded Yesterday Verdict to be Announced in Five Days 115

Xu Qizhong, the son of Xu Guannan, a wealthy merchant from Wuxing living in Shanghai, squandered money and was in debt of tens of thousands. His parents were unwilling to pay the debts on his behalf, so he applied to the First Special District Local Court for bankruptcy. Accountant Wang Sifang was appointed as the bankruptcy administrator, and creditors' meetings were repeatedly called. Most of the creditors believed that Qizhong's debts were all due to wasteful spending, and he hoped to resolve the matter through bankruptcy. Therefore, they jointly filed a criminal self-accusation against Qizhong, requesting that he be punished in accordance with the bankruptcy law. The case has not yet been concluded. Now, Ying Huizhen (also known as Wen Di Lao Si), a prostitute brothel owner, filed a lawsuit against Xu in the First Special Court to confirm the creditor's rights. Huizhen is also one of the creditors. She reported the amount of her claim and submitted three promissory notes written by Xu at the previous creditors' meetings. One was a loan of 1,000 yuan on June 25 last year, one was a loan of 4,000 yuan on July 6, and one was a loan of 5,000 yuan on July 20. However, Xu Qizhong publicly stated that although the total amount of the promissory notes was 10,000 yuan, the actual amount was only 1,000 yuan, which caused all the creditors to express doubts about Huizhen's claim and refused to recognize it. Later, the execution court of the First Special Court summoned the parties for questioning. Although Huizhen still submitted the three promissory notes as evidence, Qizhong also firmly denied it. The judge of the execution court was unable to resolve the matter and ordered that a separate lawsuit be filed to confirm the creditor's rights. Therefore, Ms. Ying hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai to formally sue Qizhong. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Yuhai summoned them for trial. The defendant was not present. The representative lawyer of the bankruptcy administrator arrived in court and stated that the bankrupt person could not leave his residence during the bankruptcy process without requesting the court's approval. Now, Xu Qizhong has temporarily returned to his hometown to repair the graves, so he did not appear in court today. However, this kind of wealthy young man does not know the difficulties of his father's entrepreneurship, only seeks to squander money, disregards the pros and cons, borrows 1,000 yuan, and signs a 10,000 yuan note. It is possible that this is the truth. In order to protect the interests of other creditors, the case should be adjourned and the defendant summoned to court for further investigation. The plaintiff's lawyer presented the promissory notes and the plaintiff's savings passbook for withdrawing money from the bank, stating that of all the loans, except for the first 1,000 yuan, which was all cash, 1,500 yuan of the second 4,000 yuan was also cash. The remaining 2,500 yuan and the 5,000 yuan of the third loan were withdrawn from the bank, and the evidence is conclusive and verifiable. After reviewing the various evidences, the court adjourned the verdict to the morning of May 5.

Sampan Boatman Dies Suddenly from Excessive Drinking Autopsy Reveals Sudden Heart Attack 116

At around 9:00 AM yesterday, a sampan boat without passengers suddenly floated to the surface of the river near the pontoon No. 67 of Puzhong in the South City. A lumberjack spotted it and brought it over. He suddenly found a dead body in the cabin, curled up inside. There was a package of fried soybeans and a wine bottle next to him. The situation was quite strange. The customs water police station was reported, and the sampan was brought back. It was found that the number was 394. It was found that it was driven by Yu Xincai from Ningbo. Yu was summoned to the police station, and he said that his sampan was rented to his cousin Yu Shunxing for driving, and pointed out that the deceased was indeed his cousin's corpse, but the cause of death was unknown. The captain then sent personnel to the dock on East Broadway Road in Hongkou and learned that Tang Shicai of Hua Yi Pengfan Hardware Store had hired him to take him to Datong Wharf and Bailianjing Ping An Shipyard in the South City at around 1:00 PM the day before yesterday. He left the boat at 5:30 PM, so it was determined that the deceased had died suddenly after drinking alcohol for dinner between 7:00 and 8:00 PM the night before. The port quarantine office was notified and sent a doctor to examine the body. The doctor found that the deceased died of a sudden heart attack due to excessive drinking. The family was instructed to prepare a coffin for burial.

Gao Zhiqing Gift Gold Lawsuit Chen Tiaoyuan Officially Sues Defendant Claims That Chen's Shares Were Paid by the 37th Division The Trial Continued Yesterday The Conclusion Awaits the Verdict on the Morning of May 5 119

Chen Tiaoyuan, the president of the Military Senate, and the late Gao Jing (Zi Zhiqing) of Liaoning were initially friendly as colleagues, and later became in-laws. They each contributed to organize the Yucheng Company, specializing in the sale of coal from the Pole Coal Mine. Gao served as the general manager of Yucheng. Later, because Chen's son was unwilling to marry Gao's eldest daughter, the marriage was canceled. The debt rights granted by Chen were naturally included in it. Recently, Chen Yinan, the representative of Yucheng Company, hired a lawyer to sue Gao Yuxiu Yun and others in the First Special District Local Court for occupying 39,000 yuan of Yucheng funds, saying that the funds were repaid by Pole after Yucheng sued him earlier and the court ruled in their favor. Gao Zhiqing included it in his estate, allowing his bereaved family to obtain illegal benefits. However, the defendant filed a defense, saying that the money owed by Dule to Yucheng had already been given to Gao by Chen Tiaoyuan. He also asked to summon Chen to court for questioning. The plaintiff's lawyer stated that Yucheng Company was actually opened by Chen alone, and requested that the name of the plaintiff's Yucheng representative, Chen Yinan, be removed, and that Chen Tiaoyuan sue in the name of the company owner. Gao Zhiqing was only the general manager of the company at the beginning. If the defendant handed over the company's capital book, it would be clearer. However, the defendant's lawyer stated that when the company was founded, the 120,000 yuan of capital contributed by Chen was from the military supply office of the 37th Division. At that time, Gao also served in the division, so this money cannot be said to belong to Chen. It is a kind of public money. The plaintiff's lawyer immediately stated that the money was paid by the 37th Division on behalf of Chen. After the two lawyers finished their arguments, the court adjourned the sentence to the morning of May 5.

Male Witch Zhang Aliu Kills People by Mistakenly Using Drugs His Intention Was Only to Cheat Money As a Result, He Was Accused 121

The male witch Zhang Aliu, 23 years old, from Shanghai, was invited to his home to watch the incense burner the day before yesterday. At that time, Zhang Aliu used the evil arts of ghosts and gods to swindle money, and prescribed medicine. After taking it, it did not improve. He was invited to his home again. After examining it, he instructed his family to buy Zijin pills (medicine name) and opium, and take them at the same time. The girl had a toxic reaction after taking it, and she became unconscious. She died at 10:00 AM yesterday. Afterwards, Dan Laohan, the maternal uncle of the deceased, 25 years old, from Dongtai, found out the situation and twisted Zhang Aliu and a small box of opium, the evidence, and turned them over to the Zhongshan Road police station. The police officer of the police station believed that the matter was related to a murder case, so he sent all the witnesses to the Caojiadu Public Security Branch Bureau for verification.

Famous Dancer Li Li Sues for Divorce From Her Husband Due to His Debts and Abandonment, Her Jewelry Pawned 122

Li Li, a former dancer at the Shanghai Metropole Dance Hall, once hailed as the "Queen of Dance," is now twenty-three years old and resides at No. 19, Lane 799, Haig Road. In 1927, when Li was only fourteen and studying in her hometown of Peiping (now Beijing), Lin Gengxin (now twenty-seven years old) from Fujian Province was also studying in Peiping. They became acquainted and, after a period of time, their affection deepened, leading to a marriage proposal. They held their wedding that year in a certain county of Shanxi Province where Lin's family resided.

Shortly after the marriage, Lin went to France to study. After Lin's departure, the family began to mistreat Li, constantly scolding and berating her. Li returned to her mother's home in Nanjing, but the Lin family refused to let her return. Driven by the need to survive, Li came to Shanghai and became a dancer, quickly gaining fame and being hailed as the "Queen of Dance."

In 1933, Li learned that Lin had returned to China after completing his studies and found him. They lived together at No. 2, Lane 744, Hart Road. However, after living together, Lin neglected his responsibilities and indulged in wandering, gambling, and debauchery. Despite Li's repeated劝告, he turned a deaf ear. Li continued her dancing career to make a living. Lin, however, did not change his ways and secretly pawned Li's jewelry, clothes, etc., dozens of times, amounting to over two thousand yuan. When questioned, he became enraged and subjected her to beatings.

On April 12th of last year, he pawned Li's diamond ring for seventy yuan. When Li confronted him, Lin pushed her violently, causing internal injuries to her right buttock bone. The injury has not yet fully healed, significantly impacting her career. Last autumn, Lin borrowed seven thousand yuan from an Indian named Amu Sen, who sued him in court, leading to Lin's arrest. Subsequently, Lin's girlfriend, a Ms. Zhu, bailed him out. Since then, Lin's whereabouts have been unknown, and the so-called Ms. Zhu, who had been residing in Li's home, also disappeared at the same time. This led to the auction of Li's residence at No. 135, Zhaonong Villa, Zilin South Road, by the local court to clear the debt. All the assets involved were earned by Li through her hard work.

Recently, due to Lin's disappearance and lack of communication, Li feels it is unbearable to continue living together. Therefore, she has engaged lawyer Huang Yiyan to file a suit in the First Special District Court, seeking a divorce from Lin and requesting alimony of two thousand yuan. As Lin's whereabouts are unknown, she requests public notification.

Yesterday morning, Judge Zhang Yuhai of the First Special Court opened a civil hearing to summon Li Li. Li and her sister went to the court. The court questioned Li about the facts, and Li provided the above details. Regarding the assault and theft of property, she cited her friend Lin Huifang (resident of No. 14, Zunde Lane, Dongyouheng Road) and her former maid Wang Jinbao (resident of No. 8, Dazhong Lane, Xietu Road) as witnesses. Lawyer Huang Yiyan submitted dozens of pawn tickets and a plaster for her injury to the court as evidence, requesting access to the case file of Lin's debt to Amu Sen (Case No. 611, 1935, Special Court). After verifying the testimonies, Judge Zhang stated that Lin Huifang and Wang Jinbao still needed to be summoned to court for testimony and adjourned the hearing to a later date.

Guo Zongwen, a native of Guangdong, had a dispute with a Russian man named Mao Kaolao Fu over jealousy on September 28th of last year at the entrance of the Metropole Dance Hall on Gordon Road. Suddenly Robbed While Urinating 135

At 12:00 AM the night before last, Zhang Shaoshan from Pudong exchanged one yuan in copper coins for a pack of cigarettes at a cigarette and paper shop on Dongxinqiao Street in the French Concession. He urgently needed to urinate and entered Baoxing Lane. Unexpectedly, two men pinned him inside the lane, and two more bandits were lying in ambush. When Zhang was still in the midst of urinating, the robbers said, "Help out with dinner money." They then snatched the copper coins and cigarettes from Zhang's hands. Zhang saw what looked like a pistol and dared not shout. Unexpectedly, the robbers pushed Zhang down, causing him to fall, and fled in different directions. When Zhang got up and left the lane, he saw two policemen passing by and reported the incident to them. However, the robbers had already gone far. As Zhang had lost little, he did not want to report the robbery to the police for investigation.

Shanghai Lawyers Association Holds Joint Meeting of Executive and Supervisory Committees, 223rd Meeting 138

The Shanghai Lawyers Association convened its 223rd joint meeting of executive and supervisory committee members at its office at No. 572, 贝勒路 (Avenue Baille) and 辣斐德路 (Route Lafayette), French Concession, at 7:00 PM last night. Committee members present included Zhang Shijie, Wei Weiqing, Yuan Yangan, Zhou Shiying, Xu Zuoliang, Wu Guochang, Zhang Juansheng, Cha Renwei, Shen Yingshi, Zhang Lan, Zhu Yakui, Dong Chi, Yu Chengxiu, Zhu Fuju, Mao Yun, Yu Ximin, Wang Manyun, Lin Kecong, Shen Junru, Jiang Yiping, Huang Zengjie, Chen Zhigao, Yang Li, Sun Zuji, Yan Yinwu, and Chen Tingrui. Shen Junru was elected as the chairman, and Dai Jixian recorded the proceedings. The meeting commenced as usual. The following items were discussed:

(A) Report Items:

* The Supervisory Committee reported on the review of the book "Modern Scribblers," regarding whether it defamed the legal system. It was deemed that the book did indeed contain content that defamed the legal system.

* Notification from the Jiangsu and other courts regarding the Ministry's order that lawyers from all provinces holding old lawyer certificates from the former Beiyang government's Ministry of Justice who have passed the review by the Wuhan National Government but have not yet exchanged them for new certificates will be allowed to exchange them for new certificates free of charge. This has been forwarded to all members for their reference.

* The Supervisory Committee reported on the review of lawyer He Zhuoxian's membership qualifications. It was deemed that there were no issues.

(B) Discussion Items:

* Regarding the book "Modern Scribblers" containing content that defames the legal system, how should it be handled?

(Decision) Send a letter to the author of the book, inviting them to attend a meeting and discuss the matter. The matter is referred to the Standing Committee for handling.

* Lawyer Gu Jiesheng's letter responding to the previous report regarding the Shanghai Local Court not summoning the parties upon arrival, stating that the date was mistakenly written by the clerk and requesting clarification and correction. (Decision) Forward the corrected report to the Shanghai Local Court for further investigation and reply. Also, send a letter to lawyer Gu reminding him to pay attention to the accuracy of the events described in the future.

* The Ministry of Judicial Administration replied that the organizational regulations for county judicial offices have already been promulgated, and there is no need to add special provisions as requested. As for the issue of lawyers concurrently holding positions in county judicial governments, it will be handled according to the actual situation after the implementation of the new system. (Decision) Send committee members Jiang Yiping and Shen Junru to Nanjing to discuss the matter with the ministry. Travel expenses will be paid by the association.

* The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce replied that it is inconvenient to jointly petition the Executive Yuan and the Ministry of Finance to correct the management of banks and money shops. (Decision) Seek the joint petition of the Shanghai Institute of Certified Public Accountants.

* The Putian Lawyers Association inquired whether it is necessary to request the Party headquarters to send personnel to guide the election of officers and whether it is necessary to follow the various procedures for people's organizations after the election. (Decision) Reply to the inquiry.

* Lawyer Zhang Shijie and others proposed to telegraph the Legislative Yuan, stating that the number of lawyers representing the National Assembly should be increased in accordance with the central allocation principle to maintain the rule of law. (Decision) Send a telegram immediately, drafted on the spot by committee members Zhang Shijie and Yan Yinwu, and notify all associations to advocate unanimously.

* Lawyer Dai Jinghuai reported that the receiving and dispatching office of the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court overcharged and abused the fee for applications and requested that the court be reorganized. (Decision) Forward to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court for reorganization.

* Lawyer Yuan Xingyun inquired whether, after a debtor declares bankruptcy under the Bankruptcy Law and the bankrupt estate has been completely distributed, creditors can still claim payment from the debtor's guarantor for the portion of the debt that has not been paid off. (Decision) As the guarantor has not declared bankruptcy, they can still assert their rights. Reply to lawyer Yuan Huihui for their reference.

* Committee member Chen Zhigao suggested purchasing inexpensive rare copies of the Complete Library of the Four Treasuries. (Decision) Purchase for 400 yuan.

* The General Assembly referred to the committee a proposal by member Chen Wenju to ban non-lawyers from performing legal duties to maintain the rule of law. (Decision) File for future reference.

* Lawyer Li Wenjie reported that concurrently serving as an auditor of Tongyi Trust Company does not hinder his legal practice and requested permission. Committee member Jiang Yiping also reported that he was appointed as a supervisor of the Jiangzhe Bank, which does not hinder his legal practice, and requested permission. (Combined Case) (Decision) Permission granted.

* Shi Da reported that lawyer Wang Jianhang's testimony procedures were incomplete and requested fairness. (Decision) Forward the letter to lawyer Wang Jianhang for a response.

* Lawyer He Zhuoxian's application for membership has been reviewed and deemed to have no problems. He should be allowed to join the association. (Decision) Passed.

* Lawyers Li Jinfu, Shen Xiangzhi, Yan Yangyu, and Hu Youhai applied for membership. (Decision) Passed.

* Committee members Xu Zuoliang and Sun Zuji proposed that the term of office for the current executive and supervisory committee members is not yet complete, and the conclusion requires time, so the date of inauguration for the new executive and supervisory committee members should be set for July 1st of this year. (Decision) Passed.

* Committee member Yan Yinwu inquired whether the travel expenses of the representative of the association attending the association meeting in an official capacity would be borne by the association. (Decision) Check the archives, and the decision will be discussed at the next meeting.

* Committee member Yan Yinwu asked whether, if he is re-elected as a standing committee member, he should still be appointed as the treasurer. (Decision) Committee member Yan will continue to serve as the treasurer.

The meeting adjourned late at night.

Deaf-Mutes in This City Initiate the Organization of the China Deaf-Mute Association 140

Mr. He Yulin and others from the deaf-mute community in Shanghai have initiated the establishment of the China Deaf-Mute Association to promote the well-being of the deaf-mute. They have received support from individuals from various provinces and cities, including Beijing, Shanghai, Hangzhou, Peiping, Tianjin, Shandong, and Sichuan, who share the same condition and have joined the ranks of the initiators. On the first of last month, they held a tea party at the New World Hotel to discuss the implementation plan.

During the meeting, Mr. He Yulin delivered a speech in sign language: "Unfortunately for us, our creators have destroyed our auditory and vocal functions, adding infinite pain and trouble to our complicated and filthy world, stripping away the happiness of life, and subjecting us to social rejection and family contempt. In order to promote the well-being of the deaf-mute community and to ensure the health of the nation and the race, we have joined hands with comrades to organize this unique deaf-mute organization, the "China Deaf-Mute Association," which has long been developed in European and American countries and Japan but has not yet been established in China. We are holding the greatest determination, the greatest courage, and the greatest sacrifice, striving and struggling to create a self-reliant movement and fight for the bright future of our happiness."

From Mr. He Yulin's speech, it is evident that the deaf-mute community not only does not abandon themselves to despair but also shares the responsibility of the nation, which is commendable. It is reported that the number of initiators has reached more than 70, and they have submitted an application to the Municipal Party Headquarters for approval. Once approved, the association will be officially established.

After the Liquidation of the Lafayette Dance Hall, Shareholders Sue to Recover Remaining Assets 142

Chen Yingjun, the former manager of the Lafayette Dance Hall, resident of No. 10, Rongfuli, Xujia Lane, Ganse Dong Road, has recently been sued in the Second Special Court by shareholders Feng Houcai and Jin Fenggang (resident of No. 315, Kulun Road, Zhabei) through their lawyer Lin Yingqing, requesting Chen to return the remaining partnership assets.

According to the court records, the plaintiffs' lawyer stated that the defendant had solicited the plaintiffs to invest in the Lafayette Dance Hall on May 1, 1934, each investing 1,800 yuan per share. Unexpectedly, after May 20, 1935, they received a notice from the defendant that the business was closing. An audit revealed that the Lafayette Dance Hall had incurred a loss of 26,953.29 yuan. Deducting this from the total capital of 41,400 yuan leaves a surplus partnership asset of 14,446.71 yuan. Dividing this by the total number of 23 shares, each share should receive 628.11 yuan. Therefore, the defendant should reimburse the plaintiffs a total of 1,256.22 yuan. Despite repeated demands, the defendant has ignored them, leading to this lawsuit, requesting that the court order the defendant to return the full amount and allow for provisional execution.

In response, the defendant Chen Yingjun stated that he had not yet returned the money because the accounts receivable had not been collected. Judge Ma Yishu concluded the debate and set a date for the verdict on May 29th.

Impersonating a Military Officer Case: Sentence Handed Down, Wang Dongyu Sentenced to One Year and Six Months 144

On February 6th, the Songhu Garrison Headquarters received a document from the Wuchang authorities stating that they had apprehended over ten individuals, including Yu Hu, in that region for falsely claiming official titles within the Xiang-E-Chuan Border Bandit Suppression Army's North Sichuan Guerrilla Force. These individuals confessed that their accomplices were hiding in the Xiafei Apartment on Xiafei Road in the Shanghai French Concession. Consequently, Yang Fengqi and Xu Pengfei, the chief inspectors of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, reported this to the French Concession police, who cooperated in apprehending Wang Dongyu, who had falsely claimed to be the commander of the 5th Brigade of the 2nd Column, as well as his secretary Yu Hou, and military supplies officer Zhang XueLi. A large number of appointment letters and insignia were confiscated. They were handed over to the Second Special Court. The police prosecuted them for disturbing public order, among other charges. The court ruled that the case was inadmissible. The police, dissatisfied with the judgment, appealed to the Third Branch of the High Court. After review, the case was remanded to the Second Special Court for retrial. Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu conducted successive interrogations and concluded the debate. Yesterday afternoon, the verdict was announced: Wang Dongyu was sentenced to one year and six months of imprisonment for forging official documents sufficient to cause harm to others. Yu Hou and Zhang Xueli were found not guilty. Yu and Zhang were released on bail of 1,000 yuan, provided by a foreign firm, pending the appeal period.

Civilized Elementary School Teacher Involved in Lawsuit; Ding Jiasheng Petitions for Retrial; Accusations of Theft May Be Cleared; Female Teacher Claims Accusation is False 145

Yu Shangxun, the principal of the Minhua Elementary School (now renamed Chunjiang) at No. 10 Shangwen Lane, Weihaiwei Road, previously reported to the Chengdu Road police that Ding Jiasheng (also known as Ding Hao), a teacher at the school, had stolen several suits of his clothing. Sun Chucheng and Others Initiate 30th Anniversary of Military Service Commemoration 146

In the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign of the late Qing Dynasty, the Governor of Jiangsu, Lu Chunjiang, recognizing the unreliability of recruitment, petitioned to implement conscription. He assigned new military officers and school officials to various counties of the Su, Song, and Tai prefectures to establish conscription bureaus and instructed local officials to formulate preferential treatment measures for conscripted soldiers to encourage enlistment. Consequently, scholars, gentry, and children of prominent families responded enthusiastically, totaling over 1,500 individuals. When these soldiers departed, all schools prepared colorful flags and celebrated their departure according to the ritual for new entrants. They were organized into three battalions stationed near Shangjin Bridge. The following year, a military academy was established. From these soldiers, one hundred were selected to study in the academy. After two years of graduation, they were assigned as officers in the 45th and 46th Schools. During the Xinhai Revolution, they were led by Governor Cheng to attack Nanjing and performed commendably. Thirty years have passed since then. Half of them have died in battle or from illness, while the survivors are scattered across various provinces and cities, having transitioned to other professions. Now, Sun Chucheng, Yu Baoying, Gao Wosheng, and others have initiated a commemoration of the 30th anniversary of their military service. They have scheduled it for the 3rd of this month at Tiger Hill in Suzhou. The day before, a preparatory meeting will be held at No. 51 Banlian Lane in the city to finalize the program for the general assembly. The preparation office for the gathering meal is located at No. 30 Jiyi Lane, Wujin Road, Shanghai. In recent days, individuals from Anhui, Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Jiangxi, and Shandong provinces have reported their attendance. It is expected to be a grand occasion.

Qiu Yuelian's Concubine Suicide Case Dismissed; Victim's Family Unwilling to Pursue the Matter 147

Qiu Yuelian, an actress in a Shaoxing opera troupe at the Sincere Company rooftop garden, cohabited with her concubine, Qiu Ye, at No. 120 Baike Road. On April 27th, at approximately 1:00 AM, Qiu attempted to persuade Ye to quit gambling, leading to a quarrel that escalated into physical violence. After being beaten, Ye, out of anger and without informing anyone, secretly ingested opium to commit suicide. By the time Qiu discovered it and sent her to the hospital, it was too late. Ye died from poisoning. The body was sent to the coroner's office, where it was determined that Qiu Ye had indeed died from poisoning. Qiu Yuelian was arrested and sent to the First Special Court. The police prosecuted her under Article 278, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Code for causing serious injury. Judge Liu Yugui had already interrogated her once and ordered her detained for a subsequent hearing. These details have been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Liu resumed the hearing in the Eighth Criminal Court. However, according to the forensic report, it was determined that the deceased had died from opium poisoning, with minor injuries to her hands and face. According to Article 277 of the Criminal Code, minor injury offenses require a formal complaint to be filed. Therefore, the deceased's mother, Ye Xia, was questioned. She stated that her daughter had married a Mr. Wu at the age of eighteen. Her son-in-law had died last June, and her daughter had been residing with her husband's family. She was unaware of her daughter's relationship with the defendant until after her death, when she was notified and went to the coroner's office to claim the body. Now that her daughter is dead and she is elderly, she does not wish to pursue the matter further. The deceased's aunt, Wu Xu, stated that she was 67 years old, a local resident living in Chong'an Lane, Haifang Road. The deceased was her daughter-in-law. After her son passed away last June 14th, her daughter-in-law claimed to be working in a yarn factory and had moved out. She had been sending her a few yuan each month. Therefore, she was unaware of her daughter-in-law's cohabitation with the defendant. Now that her daughter-in-law is dead, she also does not wish to pursue the matter deeply against the defendant, but requests that the defendant provide a certain amount of money each month for her two grandchildren's expenses. Qiu Yuelian was questioned and retained Zhou Yongding as her lawyer to represent her. Judge Liu, considering that the victim's family did not wish to pursue the case, announced in court that the case was dismissed.

Robbery and Assault: Lu Guisheng Sentenced to 14 Years 148

Lu Guisheng, a native of Pudong, gambled and recently became unemployed, unable to make a living. His cousin, Zhang Xigen, also from his hometown, lived at No. 10 Baoxing Lane, Wuzhou Road, and ran a thriving beef stall in the same road's market. His wife, Qiao, kept gold lockets and gold chains worth 300 yuan in a drawer in their bedroom. Lu, aware of these items, harbored malicious intent. At 4:30 AM on the morning of the 15th of this month, taking advantage of Zhang Xigen's absence at the stall, Lu carried a sharp knife and a rope. From the sun deck of his neighbor Gong Chuntao, also from Pudong, he used the rope to descend into his cousin Zhang Qiao's room and stole the gold locket and chain. Qiao noticed and quickly arose, holding him back and calling out his name. Lu, in a panic, pulled out the sharp knife and stabbed her five times in the head, back, and left arm. Qiao, in extreme pain, fell to the ground and cried for help. Lu immediately fled through the door. After the incident, detectives Shao Jingfan and Ye Yusi, and officer Cao Jinbiao of the Jiaxing Road police station arrested him. Lu claimed that Zhang Xigen, the owner of the beef stall, and Gong Chuntao were the instigators and that the stolen goods were stored at Gong's residence. The detectives subsequently apprehended Gong. A sharp knife and rope, discarded by Zhang Xigen, were found in his home and brought to the police station. Zhang Qiao was transported by ambulance to the Shanghai Sanatorium Hospital on Bazilu for treatment. Lu and Gong were sent to the First Special Court. After investigation, the police determined that Gong Chuntao had been falsely accused by Lu. Lu was charged with robbery, attempted murder, and false accusation. It was ordered that Lu be remanded in custody, while Gong was released on bail. Yesterday morning, Judge Jiang Shuzi resumed the hearing in the Third Criminal Court. Attorney Li Zhishan from the Municipal Council stated that the victim, Zhang Qiao, was still recovering from her injuries in the hospital and could not attend the court. The maid Jiang Aida testified and presented the doctor's medical certificate for inspection, requesting severe punishment. According to Jiang Aida's testimony, at the time of the stabbing, the master of the house fell to the ground and cried out Lu Guisheng's name. She heard the commotion, went to investigate, and saw him fleeing from the stairs. Questioned about this, Lu's confession was evasive. Judge Jiang sentenced Lu Guisheng to eight years imprisonment for robbery, ten years for attempted murder, to be served concurrently for a total of fourteen years. The remaining charges were found not guilty. The knife and rope were confiscated. Gong Chuntao was released.

Pre-Order of the Complete Book of Internal Medicine of Traditional Chinese Medicine 152

Mr. Nan Zongjing, the head of internal medicine at the Suzhou National Medical School, has recently compiled the Complete Book of Internal Medicine of Traditional Chinese Medicine. It is divided into ten sections: acute infectious diseases, metabolic diseases, respiratory diseases, digestive diseases, circulatory diseases, blood and spleen diseases, nervous system diseases, motor system diseases, and urinary and reproductive system diseases. The book includes everything from the Nei Jing, Shang Han Lun, Jin Gui Yao Lue, Qian Jin Fang, and Wai Tai Mi Yao, to books from the Song, Yuan, Ming, Qing and modern periods. It also covers the theories of famous Han physicians in the East. The book contains over 2.5 million words, over 100 categories, and over 5,000 prescriptions. It will be published in two large, exquisitely bound volumes in October, priced at $8 in legal currency. As a special offer for all sectors, pre-orders placed before the end of August (National Calendar) will be priced at only $4. In addition, a white-text joint edition of Zhang Zhongjing's Shang Han Lun and Jin Gui Yao Lue will be included as a gift (the number of copies of this book is limited; those who pre-order the Complete Book of Internal Medicine before the end of May (National Calendar) will receive this additional book first). An additional five jiao in silver dollars will be added for out-of-town postage. Pre-orders can be placed at No. 36 Daotang Lane, Suzhou.

The total amount of the convertible bond reserve is 10,807,439 yuan, including 15,646,6729 yuan and 45 fen in cash reserve, and 5,160,0730 yuan and 55 fen in guarantee reserve. April 26th, 1936, Republic of China.

Respected Editor: I have seen the news in your newspaper today (April 30th) about Sun Yin abusing and causing the death of his maid, Donglan, etc., which are all inconsistent with the facts. Ms. Sun was lonely in her family, so she adopted Donglan as her adopted daughter two years ago to accompany her. When she was adopted, the child was only five years old, so how could she be a maid? And there is evidence to check at the Household Registration Office of the Gaoqiao Public Security Branch, so the accusation that she priced and bought a maid is actually in violation of Article 296, Paragraph 1 of the Criminal Law, etc., and is actually a false accusation. That decision to be pressed for a case of injury causing death is also untrue, and the court has already investigated and issued a non-prosecution decision. The matter concerns Ms. Sun's reputation, so she is specially sending a letter to clarify the facts, and requesting that you make a correction immediately. I am extremely grateful. With deepest respect to the Editor, Sun Yin, No. 43 Shagang, Gaoqiao District, Shanghai, April 30th.

Unprecedented Spectacle in the Capital; Over Ten Thousand People Attend; World Games Football Team Performs; Chairman Lin Sends Lu Chao as Representative to Give Instructions; Ministers and Officials from Various Departments Attend to Watch the Game

(Special dispatch from Nanjing, 30th) The World Games football team, led by Shen Gangliang, arrived in Nanjing on the morning of the 30th. The Lixing Society hired cars to welcome them at the station and take them to the Society for breakfast. At noon, they went to the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum to pay their respects and lay a wreath. After the ceremony, the teams visited scenic spots such as Tan's Tomb. At noon, they attended a public banquet hosted by the Capital Party, Government, Military, Academic, and Sports Association and the Lixing Society. At 4 p.m., they were trained at the Lixing Stadium. Chairman Lin felt slightly unwell and sent Staff Officer Lu Chao as his representative to give instructions, stating that China's decision to participate in the World Games with more than 80 people was to showcase the spirit of the Chinese nation and Chinese culture to the people of the world, and wished them victory and health. After the speech, Huang Renlin introduced the "King of Football" Li Huitang to the audience, who applauded thunderously, expressing their enthusiastic welcome. It was decided that Dean Dai would kick off the exhibition match under the refereeing of Zhang Xinfu. Because the two teams, A and B, were essentially the same, there was no real competition, so the audience and the players were not particularly tense. Twenty minutes after the kickoff, Jing Guicheng of Team A scored the first goal. Li Huitang felt that his strength was not as good as before because of a recent illness, so he shot less. After resting and taking photos, the competition was fiercer in the second half. Li Tiansheng of Team A was penalized for a penalty kick. Hua Bei Hua of Team B scored a goal. Afterwards, Yang Shuiyi and Xu Wenkui of Team B each scored. Finally, Li Huitang shot on goal, accurately and powerfully, but it was blocked by Zhang Rongcai. Chen Zhenhe then headed the ball into the net, making the score 2 to 3. By the time the game was over, it was already 6 p.m. More than ten thousand people attended, making it an unprecedented spectacle for a football match in the capital. Many ministers and officials from various departments of the central government also attended to watch the game. In the evening, Dai Jitao and others hosted a banquet for the team at the Lixing Society. The entire team returned to Shanghai by night train at 10:30 p.m.

Exhibition Match Details (Dispatch from Nanjing, 30th) The World Games football team arrived in Nanjing from Shanghai on the morning of the 30th and rested at the Lixing Society before going to pay respects at the Sun Yat-sen Mausoleum. At 4 p.m., they played an exhibition match at the Lixing Stadium, divided into Team A and Team B. It was originally scheduled for Chairman Lin to give instructions before the start of the match, but Chairman Lin was slightly unwell, so Lu Chao gave the instructions on his behalf, with many words of encouragement. After Dean Dai kicked off the match, the two teams immediately made contact. Team B had a strong offensive, and the ball often revolved in Team A's area. Fortunately, the defense was effective and there were no losses. After half an hour of melee, Cao Guicheng, assisted by Feng Jingxiang, sprinted along the sideline and shot fiercely from more than ten yards to the right of the goal. Zhang Rongcai was unable to save it, and Team A scored first. Afterwards, neither side made any further gains, and Team A led 1-0 in the first half. After the break, Team B was even more active. After ten minutes, Li Tiansheng touched the ball with his hand in the goal area and was penalized for a penalty kick. Yang Shuiyi shot it into the corner of the net, tying the score at 1-1. Five minutes later, Xu Wenkui, assisted by Li Guowei, scored again. At this time, Team A's defense was in chaos. Jia Youliang crossed from the baseline and was headed into the net by Xu, making it 3-1. Team B's momentum was great. Although Team A tried to counterattack, their coordination was scattered and ineffective. Until a quarter of an hour before the end of the match, Zhuo Shijin, assisted by Jiu Guicheng, scored a goal. After that, it was still Team B's game. Jia Youliang and Xu Wenkui both broke through Team A's last line of defense, but because it was an exhibition match, they let it go lightly. Otherwise, Team A would have been defeated 5-2. When the whistle blew, Team B finally triumphed 3-2. Overall, the exhibition match was not exciting and disappointing. Apart from Feng Jingxiang and Chen Zhenhe, who were slightly pleasing, the rest of Team A were mediocre and unremarkable. On Team B, only Ouyang Kang of Nanjing had slightly inferior skills. The rest of the players were impressive, especially Jiang Shanjing, who was aggressive both on offense and defense and was praised by the entire audience. Commercial News

Gold Market Receives External Support, Resulting in a Slight Drop of One Cent; Public Debt Cleared Quite Substantially 195

Yesterday's gold market saw a drop in pure gold prices and a continued decline in the opening market. However, there were special buyers in the market taking advantage of the low prices, with significant external support. Concerns about cash withdrawals fueled rumors, leading to initial instability but eventual stabilization. In the morning, overseas silver markets reported declines in London and stability in the US. Traders indicated that there was minor buying from India after the market closed but also cited large sellers listed on the exchange. Forward silver prices in Montreux rose by 1.5 to 3.7 points. Exchange rates rose slightly. London spot gold prices declined by one penny. The Central Bank's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the UK and the US. The customs gold unit remained unchanged. The reserve requirement was posted at 11.409 yuan, a decline of 1 cent. Over-the-counter pre-market trading opened lower at 40.5 yuan. Huixiang, Tongtaichang entered the market to buy at the lower prices, pushing it up to 1 yuan. Yuanmao, Yongfuxing, Yongda, and Decheng sold off to stabilize the market. The morning opened slightly lower, and the market weakened slightly due to selling by banks. Unexpectedly, large investors took advantage of the lower prices to purchase gold bars, bringing external support to the gold market. Concerns about cash withdrawals boosted buying interest, gradually pushing prices back up. HSBC's posted exchange rates showed no change for both the UK and the US. The market stabilized. The silver balance tax was reduced by 0.25. Afterwards, there was a slight drop. Later, rumors that the cash reserve would be reduced from 60% to 40% prompted large investors to buy, causing prices to rise. However, many took profits at the higher prices, and buying interest waned as prices rose. The market trend turned flat at noon. In the afternoon market, transactions were ordinary, with alternating rises and falls. The trend gradually became uncertain. Later, with continued selling and a decline in Indian silver prices, the market remained weak. However, large investors continued to buy at the lower prices, and the final trend was stable. The swap premium rose again to 4.4 yuan, due to the impending clearance of public debt today. A record of the day's market conditions follows:

The morning opened at 1140.9 yuan, a drop of 0.3 yuan from the previous closing. Tongtaichang pushed it up to 1 yuan. Shanghai sold June US dollars at 75 cents. Tongfeng, Hengjingfu, Dadecheng, and Huixiang sold gold bars, pushing the price down to 0.07 yuan. Futai, Yongdafa, Yongfutai, Hengqiafeng, Yongtong, Taichang, and Yuanmao Yong entered the market to buy at the lower prices, pushing it up to 1.4 yuan. Four-Quarter Long-Term Loans Conclude; Coping Remains Difficult; Disputes Not Yet Resolved 197

The circumstances surrounding this year's long-term settlement have been detailed in previous reports in this newspaper. The overview as of yesterday appeared outwardly uneventful. However, a close analysis of the underlying tensions reveals the following points: Historically, Ningbo banks have extended long-term loans in Shanghai through Shanghai money shops. Therefore, repayments must also be secured by these shops. Unfortunately, this year's debtors are not merely ignoring their obligations; they genuinely lack the means to repay. Many are requesting to pay only the interest without repaying the principal. The Ningbo banks, having suffered significant setbacks in Ningbo last year, feel unable to extend loans for extended periods. Thus, they are pressing the Shanghai money shops to demand repayment, but the Shanghai shops lack the resources to cover these debts. This has resulted in a deadlock (a term in the trade for "forced execution"), causing dissatisfaction on both sides. As matters stand, forceful collection is futile. Disputes of this nature were visible everywhere yesterday. In the Shanghai financial community, a notice was issued by the Chamber of Commerce last autumn when the ten-quarter long-term loans matured, allowing a uniform extension for repayment by the four-quarter deadline next year (i.e., this year). Upon the arrival of this year's deadline, the debtors remained unable to repay. However, the financial community, having endured this extension, is now finding it extremely difficult to manage. Should further extensions be granted this year, it will be difficult to meet other obligations. Therefore, more stringent measures are necessary. These disputes will likely persist for some time. The tension within the banking and money shop industries is evident. This year, the extension of new long-term accounts is limited to those with significant latent potential. Some lenders initially agreed to extend credit but ultimately failed to honor their commitments due to environmental factors. A number of businesses have been forced to suspend operations or close down as a result. The majority of secured loans maturing this year cannot be finalized. Those able to repay both the principal and interest are considered exceptional. In most cases, borrowers cannot afford to repay either. If creditors were to dispose of the collateral through auction, they would incur significant losses. Even if tangible collateral exists, selling at low prices would result in substantial losses for the creditors. Unwilling to shoulder these losses, major negotiations are expected. In general, the conclusion of this year's long-term loans will likely be followed by a series of debt disputes. As for the long-term loans maturing yesterday, in addition to deposit portions, the money shops fulfilled their repayment obligations as usual. However, all outstanding long-term loans were generally rolled over, either transferred to current accounts or exchanged for new IOUs. Final settlements were exceedingly rare.
