May Day Commemorative Special Issue

Commemorating "May Day" and the Way Out for Chinese Laborers 217

— Lu Jingshi

"May Day" is an international labor day. Its creation was paid for by the blood and lives of workers around the world. After fifty-two years, the goals of the "May Day" movement have gradually changed, but this great day is still forever worthy of fervent commemoration by workers around the world.

On October 7, 1884, the eight major internationals in the United States (referring to the United States and Canada) and other labor organizations held a joint congress in Chicago, resolving to hold demonstrations every May 1st to demand an eight-hour workday, and a nationwide general strike. May 1st, 1886 was designated as the first demonstration day. This can be said to be the beginning of the "May Day" movement, and also the beginning of the most glorious page in the global workers' movement.

Our research shows that the European Industrial Revolution was launched independently, while the Chinese Industrial Revolution was passively forced by external forces. Because the Industrial Revolution in various European countries soon caused a panic of excess production capital and a lack of raw materials, in order to remedy this panic, the imperialists rushed to open up colonies abroad as reservoirs for domestic production capital and raw materials. China was the most ideally suited for this role and was the ideal place for imperialists. They successively invaded with their superior military, political, and economic power, utilizing their surplus capital and China's natural resources and cheap labor to create their strong nation status and obtain various illegal benefits. China itself was unable to embark on the road of industrialization due to foreign oppression, but it still could not escape the control of the imperialists. The national industry was unable to develop independently and could hardly maintain the status quo. In recent years, the near bankruptcy of major industries such as silk, yarn, and flour has been a clear example. The Industrial Revolution has not been successful, and the countryside is collapsing rapidly due to the deepening economic influence of imperialism.

So, broadly speaking, China has not yet formed a labor-capital class division. All actual distinctions, as Sun Yat-sen said, are "nothing more than big poverty and small poverty." Because both entrepreneurs and laborers suffer under the same oppression from foreign races. The cause of China's labor problem is not domestic, but the aggression of international imperialism. Therefore, the solution to China's labor problem is not a narrow class struggle, but how to overthrow imperialism. In other words, China's labor problem is the entire national problem. Only when the entire nation achieves independence and liberation can laborers achieve true happiness. This is the characteristic of China's labor problem, and it is completely different from the labor problems of other capitalist countries. We should recognize this.

The Chinese Nationalist Party is the only party in China with the most history and power to save China. The Three Principles of the People is a great strategy for the revival of China. The Three Principles of the People advocates equal treatment of all ethnic groups domestically and joint struggle with small and weak ethnic groups externally in the national independence movement. In this situation, not only must the people of the country unite and fight against foreign enemies, but also the small and weak ethnic groups must unite into a strong war front to defeat imperialism.

In addition, the Principle of People's Livelihood in the Three Principles of the People is the only key to solving China's labor problem. Its method is to control capital and equalize land rights, gradually transfer capital and land to public ownership through gradual and peaceful means, abolish private ownership, complete the social revolution, and enable the majority of people to live and work in peace and contentment, free from the threat of life panic. From this, it can be seen how much enthusiasm and determination the Chinese Nationalist Party has for saving the vast majority of laborers. Similarly, only by working hard under the leadership of the Chinese Nationalist Party can the laboring masses obtain definite guarantees.

However, we do not deny that the Principle of People's Livelihood has not yet been implemented, and the suffering of Chinese laborers has not been alleviated in the slightest, but has instead increased daily. This is not because the Three Principles of the People is ineffective, nor is it because the Chinese Nationalist Party is not working hard. It is really that the aggression of imperialism is intensifying day by day, preventing the completion of nationalism. Since the nation cannot be independent, the Principle of People's Livelihood cannot be implemented at all. This is enough to prove that if the forces of imperialism remain in China for one more day, Chinese laborers and people of other classes cannot be liberated. Only by concentrating our strength and contributing to the party, strengthening the party's actions, and realizing the party's principles as soon as possible, can the Chinese nation break away from the shackles of imperialism and achieve independence. This is the recognition and awakening that we should have when commemorating "May Day," and it is also the true way out for Chinese laborers.

The May First Movement and the International Labour Organization 218

— Cheng Haifeng

During the active development of industry in the 19th century, capitalists held all the advantages and privileges, manipulating production and distribution and treating workers' labor as a commodity, exploiting them arbitrarily. Unable to endure this, workers gradually developed a consciousness of uniting to resist. The May First Movement was conceived in this context.

The United States at that time was a newly emerging industrial nation. The years after 1873 were plagued by economic panic, unemployment soared, and the working conditions of workers deteriorated even further. On October 7, 1884, eight major international and national labor organizations in the United States convened a joint conference in Chicago, resolving that May 1st each year would be the date for demonstrations demanding an eight-hour work system, using a general strike as a method of demonstration. On May 1, 1886, the first demonstration movement was indeed held, with great success. However, more than 40,000 workers in Chicago had not yet achieved this goal and had to continue the strike to realize their demands. On May 3, workers in Chicago gathered near the McCormick Reaper Works, and the notorious Chicago Haymarket Affair occurred on that day. Although the American labor movement temporarily declined due to this incident, the spirit of the May First Movement did not disappear and spread to Europe. Therefore, in 1891, the May Day Massacre of Fourmies also occurred in France.

In 1889, the Second International (formerly known as the International Socialist Congress, now the International Labour and Socialist Party) convened its founding congress in Paris, resolving that May 1st would be International Workers' Day, designating it as a day for class-conscious workers around the world to cease work and hold demonstrations. Since then, the spirit of the May First Movement has greatly expanded beyond its original demand for an eight-hour work system, becoming a demonstration of workers' self-liberation. After several instances of bloodshed, it was finally recognized by governments around the world, and laws were enacted stipulating that work should cease on May 1st with wages paid.

Fifty years have passed since the May First Movement began in 1886. This period has included one World War, which not only provided workers in various countries with significant lessons but also awakened the governments and capitalists of various countries. This led to a greater understanding that the pursuit of social peace must begin with improving the painful lives of workers. Rather than waiting for demonstrations and bloodshed before accepting workers' demands, it would be better to gather together in peacetime to exchange opinions and achieve improvements in workers' lives through peaceful means. It was with this aim in mind that the International Labour Organization, jointly organized by governments, employers, and workers of various countries, came into being.

We know that the original demand of May First was to reduce working hours to eight hours per day. However, although a small number of countries adopted it before the European War, most countries still had not implemented it. Recognizing this, the International Labour Organization stated in its constitution: "The failure of any nation to adopt humane conditions of labour is an obstacle in the way of other nations which desire to improve the conditions in their own countries." The contracting countries also acknowledged that "all States should make an endeavour to establish a system of eight hours a day or forty-eight hours a week as the standard to be aimed at where it has not already been attained." Based on this principle, the first session of the General Conference in 1919 formulated a draft convention to promote the eight-hour system to countries around the world through international agreements. Countries that ratify this convention must earnestly implement this system.

From this, we can see that before the establishment of the International Labour Organization, the demands of workers relied entirely on their own demonstrations to obtain them. The achievements made were not only not widespread but also could not obtain thorough government guarantees. However, since the establishment of the International Labour Organization, all workers' demands can be raised at the International Labour Conference, discussed jointly with governments and employers, and international conventions can be formulated and promoted uniformly in various countries. In terms of the scope of achievements, this is naturally far greater than the achievements gained by the workers' movement in a single country or region. In terms of guaranteeing achievements, a country that ratifies a convention must enact a law to implement it. It goes without saying that the law is an ironclad guarantee. Therefore, this method of liberating workers does not require severe measures and can achieve better results, which is a significant progress.

Today, because of advancements in production technology, workers should also enjoy more leisure time. During periods of severe unemployment, working hours should be reduced to increase employment. Therefore, there is a demand for a 40-hour work week. This demand did not require demonstrations or bloodshed from workers but has already been recognized in principle by various countries. This is an achievement of the democratic International Labour Conference.

The 17th International Labour Conference in 1933 began discussing the issue of the 40-hour work week. Subsequent conferences also continued to discuss it. It was not until the conference last year (1935) that a draft convention on reducing working hours to 40 hours per week was formulated. All countries that ratify this convention should recognize: "The principle of the 40-hour week shall be applied in such a manner that the standard of living is not reduced in consequence. The adoption or facilitation of such measures as may be judged appropriate to secure this end is incumbent upon countries approving this measure. Each country shall be responsible for the implementation of this principle in various occupations in accordance with the details set forth in the convention." Currently, conventions have been formulated based on this principle, including the "Reduction of Hours of Work (Glass-Bottle Works) Convention, 1935" adopted by the 19th Conference. Similar draft conventions are currently being drafted to ensure that this reform can be universally implemented in public works, construction, the iron and steel industry, the coal mining industry, and the textile industry. The 20th International Labour Conference will be held in Geneva on June 4, 1936, to decide on the implementation of the 40-hour work week in the above industries. In addition, issues such as the printing and binding industry and the chemical industry may be included in the agenda of the 1937 conference.

In summary, the spirit of the May First Movement—liberating workers and raising the living standards of workers—can be said to be in line with the goals of the International Labour Organization. Therefore, the formulation and implementation of international conventions can also be said to be a manifestation of implementing the spirit of the May First Movement. On the one hand, the movement has progressed from the eight-hour day to the forty-hour week. On the other hand, the method has evolved from demonstrations, strikes, and bloodshed to a democratic and peaceful legislative approach. This kind of evolution can indeed be celebrated by the labor community. When commemorating May First, we should also hope that the workers of the world will jointly support this progressive International Labour Organization so that it can continue to work for the benefit of labor!

How to Commemorate Labor Day 219

— Wu Xingya

Today marks the 50th anniversary of International Labor Day.

Fifty years ago, 360,000 workers in Chicago, USA, launched a struggle to improve their lives by demanding eight hours of work, eight hours of rest, and eight hours of education. Currently, in some capitalist countries, the "three eights" system has been largely implemented, and in some countries, working hours have even been reduced to less than seven hours. The development of world industrial technology has made the demands of workers fifty years ago largely inapplicable to the current environment.

China is an industrially backward country, and the living standards of workers are obviously many times lower than those in capitalist countries. The commemoration of Labor Day in China began as late as 1920 in Shanghai. Now, sixteen years have passed since the first commemoration, and under the leadership of our Party, the lives of workers throughout China have seen significant improvements. However, these small improvements are not enough. Therefore, we must work harder to complete the tasks set by the workers of the past, the tasks they left behind.

However, we should understand that the main task of commemorating Labor Day in China at present is not simply to realize the "three eights" system. China is a country with backward living standards and a not very widespread education. In recent decades, the oppression and aggression of the great powers have prevented our national economic construction from making any major progress. After the World War, our country's main industries, such as cotton mills and silk factories, these textile industries, are clearly falling into bankruptcy and instability. The large-scale collapse of the rural economic organization and the stagnation of emerging industries have brought the national economic crisis to the point of being almost unmanageable. Naturally, in this state of industrial exhaustion, it is not easy to improve the lives of workers; it is not easy to reduce working hours. Therefore, in China, especially in Shanghai, this industrial area, there are still many workers struggling in work that is more than ten hours. Adequate education and adequate rest are even more out of the question.

In this situation, if we currently take the realization of the "three eights" system as the object of struggle, it will not be easy to achieve, and it cannot be achieved. Because China's factory capital is small, and it is also mostly in a precarious situation. If working hours are reduced, then wages will be reduced, and workers will not be able to live. If working hours are reduced and wages are increased, then the factory's output will mostly not be enough to cover costs. Therefore, the commemoration of Labor Day by Chinese workers, the commemoration of Labor Day by all Chinese people, has a different method from that of other countries, but it has the same meaning.

That is to say, the first meaning of our commemoration of Labor Day lies in developing China's national economy, improving production methods, improving production technology, and implementing labor-capital cooperation, to resist the aggression of imperialism and to promote the development and prosperity of the national economic structure. The second meaning lies in enabling all industries in the country to proceed under a systematic and step-by-step plan, so that they can develop and become rationalized. The third meaning lies in promoting production education and literacy movements, to popularize the education of the working masses. The fourth meaning lies in making all labor a kind of national service labor, all becoming an element of the Chinese nation's self-reliance.

We all understand very well; if the production technology of China's industry is not intensified and improved, and labor and capital do not earnestly cooperate, then our national industry will not be able to compete with the industry of the great powers, that is, Chinese factories will not be able to stand and develop. Therefore, Chinese workers' demand for improvement in their lives can only be achieved through thorough cooperation with factory owners and merchants. Promoting the national industry through cooperation, and promoting the rationalization of production technology through cooperation, then the factory can survive, and the lives of the labor can naturally be improved. This is the special significance of our commemoration of "May 1st" today, which must be known.

At the same time, whether education is widespread or not is directly proportional to the progress of production technology. Countries with advanced education and technology in the world, such as Switzerland, England, America, Germany, and Russia, which country is not the most advanced country in production technology? Therefore, if we want to universally realize the eight-hour education and eight-hour rest system, we must first promote the improvement of production tools and realize the increase in the quantity and quality of production materials. The development of production is the cause, and the promotion of education is the result. If we want to obtain this result, then we must regard labor as an obligation to promote the national industry and an obligation to complete the national revolution. We only fear that we do not have more physical and mental strength to contribute to the country and the nation, and not that we are shouting the slogan of completing the "three eights" system while the national industry is on the verge of collapse.

In short, Labor Day this year and today has a special meaning in China. This meaning lies in that it is not only a memorial day for reducing working hours, but also a memorial day for production and construction; it is not only a memorial day for the victory of workers, but also a memorial day for the future national victory of us. How are we going to win this memorial day? Today, we only have to work hard to produce and work hard to serve. To carry out national economic construction with the greatest strength; to strive for the development of China's national industry with the greatest effort. Only in the success of national economic construction can we truly achieve the realization of the "three eights" system, and can we truly complete the task given to us by the workers of the world fifty years ago.

Therefore, this year's "Labor Day" is the labor service day of the Chinese people, and it is the creation day of the national economic construction of the Chinese nation. Promoting this great economic construction and carrying out active labor services is the work of commemorating "Labor Day" this year and today.

Telegraphic Extra

Standardization of International Telegrams 220

— Chu Min

Today in the 20th century is truly the century of standardization. If you don't believe it, look at the standardized clocks we use—the electric clocks lining the streets—the standardized ping pong balls we play with—like those from the Huanqiu brand—and even the so-called standardized beauty. If things continue like this, everything will soon be standardized! Going a step further, if the "clocks" are standardized, the "balls" are standardized, and everything is standardized, but no one uses or plays with them, what good is the standardization? Therefore, we hope that things in the world can quickly become standardized one by one, and at the same time, we hope that people can enjoy these "standards" as much as possible, without going against the times or moving backward!

"International telegrams" are a cutting-edge communication tool of the times, and of course, they need to be standardized even more! However, "telegrams" can absolutely not be compared to "beauty." When beauty reaches old age, it can never be standardized, but "telegrams" either are not standardized, or if they are standardized, they must remain standardized. Because "telegrams" are not easily standardized, the conditions are also very demanding. At least, they must possess: 1. thorough service; 2. rapid transmission; 3. accurate text; 4. no damage to national rights.

Via CGRA, the international wireless telegraph, how beautiful are the bright red neon lights? This is the big sign of standardized international telegrams! This is also an international communication undertaking that is worthy of people's support for winning glory for the 20th century! It—CGRA—has unexpected conveniences—thorough service; it has direct circuits to various countries, the latest automatic high-speed machines, and scientific management methods—rapid transmission; it has specialists in charge of proofreading, and skilled telegraph operators responsible for reporting—accurate text; it also has extremely fair and reasonable regulations for sharing telegraphic fees, and it is purely state-owned and state-operated, free from the control and oppression of foreign forces—no damage to national rights. In short, everything about it fully meets the conditions for standardization, and it has now been supported by the general public as an authority in international telegraph routes.

The wheel of time keeps turning, we should bravely move forward! We should be the pioneers of the times, and never be content to chase after the times and lag behind! To those engaged in trade in the new era, this era is our era, not the era of old merchants who wear old glasses and only know how to write routine accounts. We should use the new weapon—telegrams—to fight for the final victory, not abandoning timely communication methods, but adopting the international wireless telegram of the era. Merchants in the new era should pay attention to the following slogans:

Long live the standardized international wireless telegraph CGRA!

Support the standardized international wireless telegraph that wins glory for the 20th century!

Not using the standardized international wireless telegraph CGRA is going against the times and moving backward!

Types of Telephone (Continued) 221

— Baozhen

Chinese Cipher Text: Any code translated using a specially compiled Chinese cipher book is called Chinese cipher text. Each character in this cipher should consist of a group of four or five numerals. A telegram whose text is entirely written in Chinese cipher or a mixture of Chinese plain language and cipher is a Chinese cipher telegram. The price per character is doubled (two jiao), which is higher than the price of plain language. Therefore, if commercial firms that use Chinese ciphers to send telegrams can compile a five-code cipher book with commonly used idioms such as "message received," "ship goods quickly," "remittance sent immediately," "stop payment on draft," "price increased, goods out of stock, ship quickly," etc., it will be more economical to send telegrams. It is very uneconomical to use four codes to represent one character. Foreign cipher telegrams often contain only three or four words, which is very brief, while the number of characters in our country's cipher telegrams is not less than the number of characters in plain language telegrams. The reason for this is probably that people do not know how to use idioms to compile ciphers.

Foreign Plain Language: Foreign plain language is written in one or more languages ​​approved for international telegraphic communication, with clear meaning, and each phrase retains the original meaning of the language used. A telegram completely written in foreign plain language phrases is a foreign plain language telegram. However, it is still considered foreign plain language in the following situations: (a) House numbers and all kinds of numbers written in Arabic numerals, with no secret meaning; (b) Telegraphic registered addresses, whether used as the name and address of the recipient or the signature of the sender; (c) Commercial logos; (d) Exchange rates; (e) Letters representing signals in signals and ship telegrams, representing signals in the International Code of Signals; (f) Common or commercial abbreviations commonly used in communications, such as Fob Cif Cat Sup lbs YMCA, etc., but only those listed in dictionaries or specially approved by the Ministry of Communications are allowed; (g) The verification words or numbers at the beginning of the text in bank and similar telegrams, up to five letters or five numerals. In addition, the compound words approved for use in English plain language telegrams should be based on the second edition of Webster's International Dictionary (Webster’s New International Dictionary Second Edition 1935).

Foreign Cipher: Foreign ciphers are divided into two types: code and cipher text. Foreign code is composed of invented words that do not contain the original meaning of the characters used, or composed of a mixture of real characters and invented words. Each word must not exceed five letters and must not contain accented letters, regardless of the method used to compose it. A telegram completely written in foreign code words, or a mixture of code words and plain language words, is called a foreign code telegram. The business identifier for international foreign code telegrams is Cdo. Cde telegrams sent between Tunis, Libya, Tangier, Algeria and other places by European and other countries are charged at 70% of the full price. Our country is part of the European and foreign system, so it is most cost-effective to use code to send international telegrams. Code telegrams may also contain plain language words or numbers and groups of numbers, but they must not exceed half of the number of chargeable words contained in the text and signature. Otherwise, they must be charged as cipher text. Those who use code to send international telegrams should pay attention to this. Foreign cipher text can be divided into two types: (a) composed of single or groups of numerals, containing secret meanings; (b) characters. words. names. or groups of letters formed, not meeting the regulations of plain language and code, but wordings composed of a mixture of numerals and letters, containing secret meanings, are not allowed to be used. Telegrams completely written in foreign cipher text, or containing cipher text, are foreign cipher text telegrams. Foreign telegrams whose text does not meet the regulations of plain language or code are also regarded as cipher text telegrams. Each word in foreign cipher text telegrams sent abroad is charged at the full price, so it is not as cost-effective to use cipher text to send international telegrams as it is to use code. (End)

Correction: The title of the previous issue was mistakenly arranged as "Types of Telephone," and it is hereby corrected.

Reasons and Methods for Hoping Telephone Users to Cooperate 222

— Ye Linsheng

The business of the telephone bureau develops with the increase of users, and users are satisfied with the rapid communication because of the complete installation and proper management of the telephone bureau. Therefore, both parties have a close relationship that cannot be separated. If the number of users decreases day by day, it will naturally have a great impact on the telephone bureau's business. If the telephone bureau does not pay attention to installation and management, then users will pay monthly fees but not get the benefit of rapid communication, and they will definitely feel very distressed. Therefore, the development of the telephone business and the speed and convenience of using the telephone are not one-sided demands, but the consistent needs of both parties. In other words: the former is not only what the telephone bureau hopes for, but also what the users agree with; the latter is not only what the users feel is convenient, but also what the telephone bureau welcomes. Business development and the convenience of using the telephone are like two rings of one thing, with interconnected relationships: there is also a relationship of cause and effect. It is difficult for a bureau whose business is not developed to have good equipment and strict management; and the result of lax management and incomplete installation will definitely not make users feel the convenience of communication, and at the same time, there will be no hope of business development.

Based on the above theory, we can know how important and essential it is for the telephone bureau and users to cooperate with each other. If both parties can cooperate, the telephone bureau can achieve the goal of business development, and users will not sigh at the waste of monthly fees; they can get the pleasure of convenient communication.

The method of cooperation is mutual, not one-sided. Here, let's first talk about the method of cooperation between the telephone bureau and users, and then talk about how users should cooperate with the telephone bureau.

A: For the telephone bureau, I think it is necessary to do the following things.

(1) The telephone bureau must be absolutely strict with the management of operators. Any events that can make users feel unhappy, such as wrong numbers, taking money during calls, and double connections, must be prevented from happening absolutely.

(2) Operators must be gentle and humble towards users, and speak politely.

(3) When users have questions, the information desk must answer truthfully, even if the matter is not within the scope of the answer, it should be answered as much as possible.

(4) In addition to explaining the reasons truthfully when users question, if the fault lies with the operator, it should be open and honest and tell the user how the operator will be punished.

(5) If the telephone is damaged, repair it immediately (except at night). If it can be proven that the damage to the machine is unintentional, the situation should also be considered and appropriate measures should be taken.

(6) Personnel should be sent to the telephone installation locations of users to inspect and if users have dissatisfaction or misunderstandings, the inspectors are responsible for explaining. Sometimes they can try calling the telephone on the user's machine to verify the performance of the operator's connection in the bureau.

(7) A "User Report Form" should be printed and distributed. The form should be divided into several grids "For example: Speed of connecting calls", "Politeness of language", "Any wrong connections or taking money during calls" and other inconvenient places... Users should be asked to fill out and send one copy every quarter or half a year, and the bureau can use this as the basis for individual improvements.

(8) Users are welcome to send people to the bureau for on-site investigation, so as to eliminate all misunderstandings and enhance the friendship between the two parties.

B: For users, the following things should be done:

(1) Users should use the telephone in accordance with the methods stipulated in the telephone directory.

(2) Automatically restrain the talking time, do not be too lengthy, so as not to hinder others from calling this user and waiting for a long time.

(3) When a telephone failure occurs, or it is suspected that someone is playing with it, notify or question the place notified as shown in the directory.

(4) If there are any unsatisfactory events, please do not scold on the machine, but notify the responsible personnel of the bureau in writing or verbally.

The above is just a list of a few points, and of course, there are bound to be omissions. If both parties have the sincerity to cooperate, a satisfactory result can be achieved.

Methods to Avoid Damaging Submarine Cables 223

— Hua

Please pay special attention, ship owners

In recent months, submarine cables between Shanghai and Nagasaki, Shanghai and Yantai, and Qingdao and Sasebo have been damaged by fishing boat anchors, leading to frequent repairs and communication disruptions. Although the Ministry of Communications has requested the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to strengthen protection measures, the vastness of the sea and the large number of fishing boats make it difficult to implement effective protection in practice. Therefore, the maintenance of submarine cables depends on ship owners understanding and avoiding methods that cause damage. Recognizing this, our national telecommunications authorities have previously printed promotional pamphlets detailing methods to avoid damaging submarine cables, available for public request. The reporter now extracts key points for publication, hoping that ship owners will pay close attention and jointly maintain the safety of communications.

Methods to Avoid Colliding with Submarine Cables

(A) If a ship knows the location of a submarine cable, it must not anchor within a reasonable distance of the cable and must not lower fishing gear. Information on the location of cables within China's territorial waters can be obtained from waterline companies or the local telegraph office. These agencies also provide maps of submarine cable locations to ship owners free of charge. Ship owners who have not yet obtained these maps are urged to do so promptly.

(B) Ships must not approach or lower fishing gear within one nautical mile of a cable repair ship. According to international maritime regulations concerning such ships, repair ships must display prominent markers on the mast, consisting of two red balls (or red lights) suspended horizontally, with a white ball (or white light) in the middle. They must also display warning lights above the captain's navigation room during cable repairs to ensure caution. (To be continued)

Q&A Column 224

This publication has created a Q&A section. Members of the public are welcome to inquire about unclear aspects of telegram and telephone sending and receiving procedures, telecommunications regulations, or any telecommunications knowledge. This publication welcomes and answers inquiries.

(1) Dai Hongsheng, Tunxi, asks: I recently heard that domestic magnet-type telephone sets are available. Where can I buy them? Our business plans to purchase one. Please advise.

(Answer) Zhongtian Electric Factory at 45 Shandong Road, Special District No. 1, Tianjin, sells domestic magnet-type telephone sets. Please inquire directly for pricing.

(2) Mr. Yan Minzhi, Huaining, asks: Regarding Article 102 of the domestic telegraph business rules, "When sending two or more telegrams at the same time, only one special delivery fee is charged, but this does not apply if they are not addressed to the same recipient." If two telegrams are delivered simultaneously to individuals A and B within the same store, is only one special delivery fee charged, or are two still charged?

(Answer) According to regulations, if the telegraph bureau delivers special delivery telegrams to individuals A and B within the same shop or residence, and they are not the same recipient, two special delivery fees should be charged.

(3) Mr. Huang Zixing, Changsha, asks: If a sender includes a few difficult-to-translate words in a Chinese telegraph and the telegraph bureau must translate them, how will the fees be charged?

(Answer) All words translated by the telegraph bureau will be charged a translation fee per word, in accordance with regulations. For example, if the telegraph bureau translates two words, a translation fee of two cents will be charged.

Shen Bao Literary Supplement

The Hardness of Literature 225

— Qin Wen

"Literature is soft."

In the past, people often said and wrote this.

Regardless of whether this statement is correct, hardness and softness are simply matters of nature, without any good or bad relationship. As Zhuangzi said, "Everything has its own rightness, everything has its own suitability." Hardness has its uses, and softness also has its needs. Gold is more expensive than copper, not entirely because its color is more brilliant and pleasing, but because it has toughness and can be stretched. Although this is not a good example of gentleness overcoming strength, it is clear proof that "soft is not necessarily bad."

Generally speaking, the hardness of a play is higher than that of a novel. Although plays no longer need to strictly adhere to the "three unities," time and place must be consistent within the same act or scene; much artifice is required, resulting in a rigid outcome. Poetry is essentially verse, and its sound is harmonious when read aloud. If the rhyme is not properly adhered to, it feels stiff, indicating that poetry should be soft, so its hardness is even lower.

In terms of schools of thought, the hardness of naturalist works is higher than that of romantic works because naturalists emphasize reason, while romantics rely on emotion. Naturalism seeks to be scientific, while romanticism emphasizes ideals; "reason" and "science" are both strict, so they are naturally harder.

Focusing solely on novels, from a writing perspective, novels written in third person are harder, while autobiographical novels are relatively softer. In autobiographical novels, even if the author is not the protagonist, they are always a part of the scene. Pretending to write based on personal experiences, they create an invisible center, reporting in a gentle and roundabout manner, making it easy for readers to sympathize, thus making it softer. Authors of third-person novels stand in the position of an observer, and their attitude is inevitably calm and strict, so it is naturally harder.

Literature is "the expression of personality." The hardness or softness of a work is directly proportional to the author's personality. Under this condition, it can be said that the output of female writers is generally lower in hardness than that of male writers—this is, of course, a generalization.

Writers are "products of their environment," and "local color" is highly relevant, so Western literature differs from Eastern literature. Comparatively, Western literature is harder—emphasizing reason, focusing on "fragmented descriptions"; Eastern literature is softer. "Timeliness" is also highly relevant. Ancient literature is softer because it is mostly a product of romanticism, while modern literature is harder—new literature is Europeanized, not only in China, but also in Japan.

"Nationality" plays an important role in the color of literature. This does not hinder the expression of the author's personality; it is a mutually causal continuation. Therefore, within the West, German literature has its own characteristics, and French literature has its own characteristics; in the East, Chinese and Japanese literature also have their own characteristics. From a nature perspective, German literature always feels harder than French literature, and Russian literature is naturally even harder, probably because of the cold climate, difficult living conditions, and the serious attitude of the authors.

Even within the works of a single author, the hardness varies. Generally, joyful moods are soft, while sorrowful moods are hard. Or, it may be that if one is casual, the hardness of the work is low; but if one is "stimulated by national crisis" and becomes serious, the hardness increases—at least, some people say this, and some people write this.

The Miser 226

— Liu Ming

——Short Chronicles of Borderland Characters——

"What's this?"

"Oh, it's shoes."

The son saw his father rummaging through the box he brought back from school, holding things that the old man shouldn't see, and his face flushed.

"Shoes? Are shoes like this?"

"Dad, these are made of leather."

The father didn't look at the shoes, but directed his displeased gaze straight at his son's face.

"How much? Is this how you spend the money I give you? Huh?"

"Dad, they're not expensive, just, … only one dollar, only a bit more than cloth shoes… only thirty cents more."

The son forced a smile as he answered, completely concealing the actual price.

"This is still cheap? This is… let me try them on!"

The old man's expression softened, and as he said this, he sat down on the bamboo chair, wiped the muddy soles of his feet a few times with his sleeve, and put on those black and shiny contraptions.

"Ah, they fit perfectly, as if you bought them for me."

The old man made a sound of praise.

The son saw the dirty feet going into the shoes, secretly worried, but couldn't say anything, so he put on a flattering appearance and said,

"Dad, don't rush, let me fetch you a basin of water, do they fit? You can wear them from now on, I'll get another…"

"I'll wear what?" The old man put on one shoe and stood up, tilting his head, examining them with his eyes: "Aren't these hard to walk in?" A look of sudden recollection appeared on his face, "Ah, they look like boots from years ago!"

The mother was tidying the washed clothes in the next room, and when she heard the old man examining the things her son brought home, she worried that he would pursue the source of the money, implicating her, the old mother who had secretly given money to her son. When she realized that the old man was happy, she picked up a bundle of blue cloth clothes and folded them, and then walked to the door with a smiling face and said,

"Aren't you going to be a guest tomorrow? Your son gave them to you, so enjoy the blessing, right?"

"Young people care about appearance… I like that they're sturdy!" The old man bent down, using his fingers to feel the leather a few times, "What kind of leather is this? I don't think cowhide is this soft!"

"Dad, this is tanned leather, made with foreign methods."

The son replied while flashing a triumphant look at his mother, as if to say: I've tricked the old man this time.

The mother, standing behind the old man, puckered her lips and raised a finger to her son.

The old man, hearing that they were made with foreign methods, gently put down the shoes, put on a serious face, and said,

"In the future, don't buy any foreign goods!"

Then, he placed his hands behind his back and walked out the door. Just as he crossed the threshold, he turned back, with a loving expression, and instructed,

"Pick them up carefully!"

The mother saw the old man leave, and then complained to her son:

"Don't be so happy! You need to be more careful next time. Also, you should also put away those bottles and cups of yours!"

"It doesn't matter! I know how to trick him now, unlike before…"

The son immediately began to hum a little tune.

The next day, the old man was going to be a guest, and looked at the patched-up worn shoes his wife had repaired, frowning and saying:

"Aren't there any without patches?"

The wife understood his meaning, and grabbed the son's leather shoes and threw them in front of him.

"You have ready-made ones, and you don't wear them? … What new shoes do you want?"

At the same time, she threw the patched cloth shoes under the bed.

The old man didn't speak, and slowly put on the leather shoes. Suddenly, he remembered something, and immediately took them off again.

"What? You're not going to wear them?"

"Why wouldn't I wear them? … But, do you want me to wear them all the way there? Let the stones wear them out, good idea!"

The old man put on a new blue cloth suit, carried one leather shoe in each hand, and walked barefoot towards the fields.

The wife saw her son standing nearby with a pout, and said,

"You're afraid he'll wear them out? … He treasures them very much! … You should let him be happy for a while, then he'll be happy to give you school money.… The poor old man!"

In the afternoon, the old man came back barefoot as usual, but he wasn't carrying the leather shoes in his hand.

The wife asked in surprise,

"Ah, the leather shoes?"

The old man was already tipsy, smiling and finding a stool to sit down.

"You'll never guess, today… Pour me a cup of tea, the vegetables are too salty!"

"Did you lose them? … You don't look like you did! … Oh, you drunkard, you're hiding them and playing with us!" The wife rolled her suspicious eyes, slipping them towards the old man's waist. Then she turned her head, pointed her mouth, "I don't like guessing, your son bought them back for you, if you lose them, not to mention he'll be sad, I won't let you get away with it!" Then she said to her son: "Go pour him a cup of tea, … he won't lose yours, if he loses them, I'll make him pay you back."

The son, looking depressed, reluctantly agreed and went to pour tea.

"Don't rush, after drinking tea, listen to me, … I was very thirsty along the way… The water in the rice paddies really doesn't taste good, it has a muddy smell, … Look, that Chen Santouzi was there too."

"Which Chen Santouzi?"

"Oh, have you forgotten? … That Chen Santouzi who wastes money, can't you remember him? … I'll tell you, once, someone brought a cow to sell to him, asking for fifty yuan. He squinted his eyes and glanced at it, turned around and walked away, shaking his hand and saying, I don't want it, I don't need one for fifty yuan, what am I going to do with it…? Bring me a good one, then I'll buy it! … In our eyes, one for fifty yuan is already very expensive, but he looked down on it! Later, they figured out his temper, and reworked that one worth fifty yuan, brushing its fur, and oiling its hooves and horns, and brought it again… Master Chen, this is a top-quality one, even if you search with a lantern, you won't find another one! … See how our Master Chen reacted, this time he looked at it again and again, from head to tail.… How much do you want?… How much? Master Chen, we wouldn't dare to take advantage of you, eighty yuan, not a penny less.… See how Master Chen reacted, again from tail to head, pretending to be unhappy and scolding, Nonsense, how can it be so expensive, you can't fool these people's eyes. Seventy yuan at most!… See, he still says his eyes are good, really made of bodhi seeds.… So the people replied to him, Master Chen, how would we dare to deceive you, to tell you the truth, we'll be struck by lightning if we overcharge you.… This fellow with clouded mind then said, Okay, leave it with me!… Haha, today he was also there as a guest."

The old man said to this point, saw his son bring tea, and while taking the teacup, stared at his son and asked,

"Why not? What would I gain by deceiving you? You gave me the money after all, and it was a certain amount. Where would I get more money to spend?"

The son pretended to be telling the truth.

"Yes, I also know, you don't have extra money to waste."

The old man nodded, then buried his head and drank tea.

The son then flashed his mother a triumphant look.

The wife urged the old man, saying:

"You drunkard, don't just babble, … tell me, where are the shoes? Did someone borrow them from you?"

"Where? Would you be willing to lend them out! Those kinds of shoes." The old man acted slightly reproachful, "These shoes are really strange, when you walk, they squeak, squeak, even before you enter the door, eight or nine heads stick out and shout: Oh, what's that sound!… Oh, foreign shoes!"

Then, he drank a mouthful of tea.

"That fellow Chen Santouzi grabbed me, … Aha, old man, you've become fancy too. How much did they cost? How much? I said: You guess, you guess,… Eight yuan,… Wrong, you guessed wrong.… Then, nine yuan.… Ugh, that foreign devil's thing, he really tricked him."

He took another sip of tea.

"They're really using salt like it's worth more than rice, the vegetables were so salty!… Later, I said to him, only thirty cents more than cloth shoes, one yuan.… One yuan? I'd be willing to pay three yuan! He was completely shocked. I said, are you really willing to pay? I didn't expect him to really take out three yuan. That fellow with clouded mind!"

"What, you really sold them?"

The wife widened her eyes.

"No? With so many guests, would I be willing to make you look bad! I said to him, I don't want to make money, why would I sell them? Then I said a polite thing, I could give them to you, but selling them? I'm really embarrassed…"

"What, old thing, you just gave them to him like that?"

The wife became a little anxious. The son looked even more uneasy.

"I'm not that stupid! An item worth one yuan, not like I stole it for free. That's worth five dou of grain. When I said that, I was afraid that the fellow would say, Okay! Just give them to me then. Everyone knows he's not very polite. I quickly continued, I don't like wearing foreign devil things. These are my kid's, he was unhappy wearing them today!"

The wife pursed her lips and smiled.

"You're really a sly old fox!"

"Ugh, you still say I'm a sly old fox! I was just a little too honest today. I said, it would have been good if they were bought for five yuan!"

The old man then took out three silver dollars.

"Ah, did you actually sell them? In front of so many people?" The wife immediately took a step towards him, asking with wide eyes, almost scolding, "Your skin is really… really thick!"

"There's no way around it! You don't know, Chief Zhang was also advising me. Think about it. How could I not agree to what he said?… That old monster often opens his mouth and it's all about donations, taxes, estimating and digging into your pocket, not leaving you any leeway. Today he was suddenly nice to me, leaning close to my ear and smiling: Sell them, it's good to sell them, earn two big yuan, and you can have your son buy another pair! I also calculated in my heart, not bad, the price of one shi of grain. I didn't care if people laughed or not, I just said that the chief ordered me to, so I had to obey. Really, if it wasn't for the chief speaking, who would be willing to lose face in public, especially since they were all laughing in such a strange way."

The son turned green with anger, and immediately walked towards the room.

"Stupid thing, are you angry? Come, I'll give you one, and go buy another pair!"

The son had no choice but to endure his anger, turned around and took it, but after walking a few steps away, the old man called out:

"Turn around, I'll give you another one… Buy another pair for me too!"

"What are you buying them for? Don't spend money carelessly!" The wife knew the actual price of the shoes and hurriedly stopped him, "If you don't have new shoes to wear, I'll make them for you!"

"No, I don't necessarily want to wear them, it's just that I'm afraid there are no other fools willing to pay three yuan to buy them."

The old man stood up, gave the silver dollars to his son, and walked away.

The son was so angry that he stamped his feet, narrowed his throat, and muttered in a low voice,

"It's really seeing a ghost! You old fool, people are selling them for eight yuan a pair!"

"Only eight yuan, didn't you tell me ten yuan!"

The wife asked the son in surprise.

The son's face turned red, and he stammered,

"Didn't I say ten yuan?"

"Hmm, you're all lying to me about the price! I really don't know, what a big waste you young people are!"

The wife pursed her lips unhappily.

That Boatman 227

— Fei Er

When I returned to Singapore again, I immediately ran into the boatman who had once taken me off the ship. He warmly welcomed me, saying:

"You really came back! Good! Good! It's hard to be a human, but it's also happy to be a human!"

In the afternoon, after he finished work, he pulled me to a nearby coffee shop, saying:

"Let's have a cup of coffee. I told you, there are good coffee shops in Middle Street."

The coffee shop was still so crowded; various words, various characters, and various smokes.

I saw a fresh scar on his forehead, which hadn't yet scabbed over, and asked:

"Have you been fighting again recently?"

"Ha, ha, fought a bit. Very refreshing."

"What happened?"

"It's a small matter," he pulled out a cigarette and smoked it, then continued. "You know those sampan hands on the sea, the dock and the sea are in the palm of their hands. 'Newcomers' from the mountains will be cheated if they are not careful. Alas, forget it, forget it. Shanghai is at war, but they are smuggling × goods. Once I saw it, I said:

"Bay! What are you doing illegally? You'll earn any black or white money!"

"None of your business!" one of them said.

"Mind your mother's business!" A fist came out of my hand. That one fell into the boat, and several others climbed out from the stern and the cabin, holding wooden sticks. I was all alone. Running was the best option. Just as I picked up the oar, the first person struck my right forehead with a wooden stick. Annoyed, I grabbed his stick with force and swung it out. That one also fell; they all rushed over in a swarm. I grabbed the oar and rowed nimbly. Spitting a mouthful of saliva on the second person. Haha! They cursed behind me. Is that heavy wooden chicken as nimble as my little duck? Haha!"

"But you're bleeding." I said.

"What's the big deal. I've been in 'Mata Cu' prison and fined. What's a big deal?—Ha ha, how is Penang?" He looked at me.

"Nothing much. Everyone is complaining." I said.

"Complaining? What's so great about that. A person always has a way. Are they going to starve to death?"

"They can't compare to you!" I laughed.

"Me? What's so great about me. I was driven out of my hometown by the gentry; not allowed to return. When I caught shrimp, I ran into the shrimp hut closing; when I opened a mine, I ran into people being laid off. What's so great about me."

"You can carry four or five hundred catties of goods; you can row a boat," I added, "you can also fight!"

"Alas, alas, forget it, forget it. The boss said to me: "From now on, don't go to sea; you can carry goods well. You always like to cause trouble." I said, "Okay, anything is fine." So now I'm not a boatman, but a cargo carrier."

The coffee shop was hot, the workers swallowed a piece of bread in one bite, laughing loudly. Shop assistants, managers, and young bosses were sipping coffee, discussing things in low voices.

He looked at me and said again:

"The manager warned me: "Don't cause any trouble, do your job well, lest you lose your job." What am I afraid of? Haven't I lost my job before? Even if I lose my job, so what? These days, it's enough not to starve to death. I won't starve to death, so I'm not afraid, I'm not afraid."

The sea nearby, the ship's whistle was sounding. He then remembered,—

"A few days ago, some fishermen from Sarawak came out to Singapore, they were preparing to return to

"Tangshan." They said: "Damn, the fish have all been caught, and the salted fish are worthless. Everyone is going back to Tangshan to starve."

""Starving is the same everywhere, isn't it?" I said.

"They didn't say anything. They seemed to have no idea what to do. Poor people! I thought:

""Why do people starve? Why do people starve? If it were me, I would—""

"What would you do?" I asked.

"What? I'd live by fighting; after fighting, I'd go to jail to find food. After coming out, I'd fight again, and after fighting, I'd go back to jail. What's the big deal?"

"Ha, ha, ha, I didn't expect you to be a natural fighting machine!" I laughed loudly.

"I'm not just a fighting machine," his face suddenly became serious, showing that he wasn't joking. "I'm also a rowing machine, a cargo-carrying machine, a machine for the gentry and bosses to vent their anger on!"

A small cigarette butt was thrown on the ground, and the remaining fire was still emitting smoke.

A shop assistant came over and shouted:

"Stop talking nonsense. Talking crazy all day long. "Xinji" (ship name) is here, go to work!"

So, he poured the remaining coffee in the cup into the saucer and drank it dry in one gulp.

Then, this dark face, strong body, broad and prominent forehead, tousled hair, thin gauze shirt, and shorts disappeared from my eyes. Leaving behind that forehead scar, and those pungent words, mixed in the chaotic water vapor and smoke, swirling in my mind.

Song of the Stars 228

— Wang Yaping

Our names are Stars,

Like spring flowers and autumn trees on earth,

Decorating the beautiful night sky.

We are the descendants of light,

The sun is our father,

The moon is our mother,

We have eternal life,

And an undying spirit that lasts ten thousand eons,

Standing high in the sky at night,

Casting a sparkling light upon the earth.

I love the still, windless lake,

The deep, boundless ocean;

I love the biting, invigorating cold wind of winter,

The nightingale's clear, fluent singing;

I love even more the dazzling myriad lights,

Which shoulder the same mission as we do,

Burning with heat, and great power,

Revealing light in the darkness.

Dark clouds are our enemies,

They often shade the azure sky,

The moon's face, and our eyes.

But we have never once surrendered,

Because we foresaw their weak life,

Like the embers of oriental fireworks,

A flash and they vanish without a trace.

When the east sky flashes with brilliant dawn,

We all hide in the heavenly palace to sleep,

Sometimes dreaming of the beautiful human world

And playing with lively, innocent children,

Sometimes dreaming of dark, hungry demons,

Exhausting all their strength in desperate struggles,

At dusk, the western sky is dyed with colorful clouds,

We rise from the twilight to our heavenly seats,

Following the beautiful moon maiden,

Happily, we begin our diligent work.

Thus, holding up lanterns in the dark night,

Never with weariness, or fear,

The sorrow of fools, and the terror of life and death,

Our names are Stars, cultivating the eternity of life in endless,

unceasing motion.
